# PART I: STRATEGY DOCUMENT

## SECTION 1 — EXECUTIVE VERDICT

**What Recall Touch should actually be:** The Revenue Execution OS — an AI-powered system that ensures no business opportunity dies from poor follow-up, missed communication, or human delay. Not a generic AI receptionist. Not a chatbot. Not a CRM. It is the execution layer that sits between your existing tools and your revenue — making sure every inbound lead gets answered, every follow-up happens on time, every no-show gets recovered, every dead lead gets resurrected, and every quote gets chased.

**What it should NOT be:** A general-purpose AI assistant, a full CRM replacement, a marketing automation tool, or a cheap answering service. It should never compete on "we're the cheapest AI calls" — that is a race to zero margin.

**Where it can realistically win:** The massive, underserved space between "CRM that logs data but doesn't act" and "human staff that costs $4,000/month and still misses calls." Local service businesses (dental, HVAC, legal, med spas, roofing, real estate) feel this pain most acutely. They lose $5K-$50K/month in missed calls, forgotten follow-ups, and no-show appointments. They cannot afford full-time staff for every gap, and existing tools (Calendly, HubSpot, generic AI bots) don't execute — they just organize.

**Strongest path to 9 figures:** Vertical-by-vertical domination of local service businesses ($297-$2,400/mo ARPU), expanding into multi-location and franchise operations ($5K-$25K/mo), then white-labeling to agencies/resellers (thousands of sub-accounts). The wedge is "answer every call, recover every missed opportunity" for single-location service businesses. The expansion is "become the revenue execution backbone for every service business in North America."

**Highest-probability wedge:** Single-location home services and healthcare businesses (dental, med spa, HVAC, plumbing, legal intake). They have urgent pain (missed calls = lost revenue NOW), budget ($297-$497/mo is trivial vs one recovered job), fast onboarding (phone number + business hours + greeting = live in 10 minutes), and clear ROI proof (X calls answered, Y appointments booked, Z revenue recovered).

**Highest-upside wedge:** Multi-location franchise operations and the agency/reseller channel. A single franchise deal = 50-500 locations × $500/mo = $300K-$3M ARR from one contract. The agency channel creates distribution leverage — 500 agencies each managing 20 accounts = 10,000 paying accounts without direct sales cost.

**Standalone vs acquisition:** Build for standalone scaling with acquisition optionality. The most attractive acquirers (ServiceTitan, Podium, Housecall Pro, Mindbody, Toast, or even Twilio/Vonage) want to buy what they can't easily build: a working AI execution layer with proven vertical expertise, embedded customer workflows, and real revenue data. Building standalone to $20-50M ARR makes the company attractive at 10-15x revenue for a strategic acquisition ($200M-$750M+).

---

## SECTION 2 — CATEGORY CREATION

### Category Options Evaluated

**1. Follow-Up OS**
- Strengths: Clear, actionable, solves a universal pain
- Weaknesses: Sounds reactive; "follow-up" feels like a feature, not a platform
- Memorability: 7/10
- Enterprise credibility: 5/10
- Consumer clarity: 8/10
- Expansion flexibility: 6/10

**2. Revenue Recovery OS**
- Strengths: Directly ties to money; CFO-friendly language
- Weaknesses: Implies the business is broken/losing money (slightly negative framing)
- Memorability: 7/10
- Enterprise credibility: 7/10
- Consumer clarity: 7/10
- Expansion flexibility: 5/10 (hard to expand beyond "recovery")

**3. Revenue Execution OS**
- Strengths: Proactive, premium, implies systematic execution; covers inbound, outbound, follow-up, recovery, booking, reactivation. Sounds like infrastructure, not a feature.
- Weaknesses: "Execution" is slightly abstract for very small businesses
- Memorability: 8/10
- Enterprise credibility: 9/10
- Consumer clarity: 6/10
- Expansion flexibility: 9/10

**4. Opportunity Capture Platform**
- Strengths: Positive framing, implies value creation
- Weaknesses: Sounds like lead gen; doesn't convey the execution/automation aspect
- Memorability: 6/10
- Enterprise credibility: 7/10
- Consumer clarity: 6/10
- Expansion flexibility: 6/10

**5. Revenue Autopilot**
- Strengths: Extremely clear value prop; implies hands-off operation
- Weaknesses: "Autopilot" has trust issues (Tesla association); implies no control
- Memorability: 9/10
- Enterprise credibility: 5/10
- Consumer clarity: 9/10
- Expansion flexibility: 7/10

**6. Communication Execution Infrastructure**
- Strengths: Very enterprise, very defensible positioning
- Weaknesses: Too abstract for SMBs; sounds like Twilio not a product
- Memorability: 4/10
- Enterprise credibility: 10/10
- Consumer clarity: 3/10
- Expansion flexibility: 10/10

### CHOSEN CATEGORY: Revenue Execution OS

**Tagline hierarchy:**
- Primary: "The AI Revenue Execution System"
- Secondary: "Every call answered. Every follow-up executed. Every opportunity captured."
- Tertiary: "Stop losing money to missed calls, forgotten follow-ups, and no-shows."

**Why this wins:** "Revenue Execution" is proactive (not just recovery), premium (not cheap automation), expandable (covers calls, follow-ups, bookings, reactivation, campaigns, quotes, invoices), and enterprise-credible while still being comprehensible to a plumber who misses 30% of inbound calls. The word "execution" differentiates from tools that organize but don't act. Every competitor is a "platform" or "tool" — Recall Touch is the system that actually does the work.

---

## SECTION 3 — TOTAL MARKET MAP

### Market Landscape

The total addressable market sits at the intersection of three massive categories: business communication ($40B+), CRM/sales automation ($65B+), and vertical SaaS for service businesses ($25B+). Recall Touch targets the execution gap — the space between tools that organize data and staff that act on it. This gap represents approximately $18-25B in annual spend across North American service businesses alone.

The market breaks down into three tiers by timing, urgency, and readiness to adopt AI execution:

### Tier 1 — Immediate Wedge (Months 1-6)

**ICP 1: Single-Location Home Services (HVAC, Plumbing, Electrical, Roofing, Restoration)**
- Pain: Miss 30-60% of inbound calls during jobs. Each missed call = $200-$5,000 lost job.
- Promise: "Never miss another service call. Your AI answers when you can't."
- Outcome: 40+ additional calls answered/month, 15+ appointments booked, $8K-$30K recovered revenue
- Features required: AI phone answering, business hours, greeting, appointment booking, call summary/transcript, SMS follow-up
- Why they churn: AI sounds robotic, can't handle complex questions, no proof of ROI
- What makes them stay: Dashboard showing "$X recovered this month," real appointment bookings, call recordings they can review
- Best offer: "Try free for 14 days. If we don't book you at least 5 new appointments, cancel with no charge."
- Pricing: $297-$497/mo
- CAC: $80-$200 (Google Ads "AI answering service for plumbers", Facebook retargeting, ServiceTitan/Jobber integrations)
- Ease of sale: 9/10
- Urgency: 10/10
- Budget: 8/10
- Onboarding speed: 9/10
- ROI proof: 10/10
- Retention: 8/10
- Virality: 7/10 (trade associations, contractor groups)
- Support burden: 5/10 (non-technical users need hand-holding)
- Expansion: 7/10 (add locations, add outbound, add campaigns)

**ICP 2: Dental & Medical Practices**
- Pain: Front desk overwhelmed, 25-40% of calls go to voicemail, patients leave for competitors
- Promise: "Your AI receptionist answers every patient call, books appointments, and sends reminders — 24/7."
- Outcome: 20+ additional appointments/month, 90% reduction in no-shows, zero hold time
- Features required: AI phone, appointment booking with calendar sync, appointment reminders, recall/reactivation (overdue patients), insurance FAQ handling
- Why they churn: HIPAA concerns, integration complexity with practice management software
- What makes them stay: Patient reactivation ("We reactivated 47 overdue patients this month"), no-show reduction proof, front desk workload reduction
- Best offer: "See how many appointments you're missing. Free 14-day audit."
- Pricing: $497-$2,400/mo (scales with providers/locations)
- CAC: $150-$400
- Ease: 7/10, Urgency: 9/10, Budget: 9/10, Onboarding: 6/10, ROI: 9/10, Retention: 9/10, Virality: 6/10, Support: 6/10, Expansion: 9/10

**ICP 3: Legal Intake**
- Pain: Potential clients call once and if not answered, call the next lawyer. Every missed intake call = $3K-$50K lost case.
- Promise: "Never lose a case to a missed call. AI intake specialist, 24/7."
- Outcome: 30%+ increase in qualified intake, faster response time, after-hours capture
- Features: AI phone with legal intake scripts, conflict check prompts, urgency triage, CRM push, follow-up scheduling
- Why they churn: AI can't handle nuanced legal questions
- What makes them stay: Case value tracking, intake-to-retained conversion proof
- Pricing: $497-$2,400/mo
- CAC: $200-$500
- Ease: 7/10, Urgency: 10/10, Budget: 10/10, Onboarding: 6/10, ROI: 10/10, Retention: 8/10

---

## SECTION 4 — ICP PRIORITIZATION

### Tier 2 — Medium-Term (Months 6-12)

**ICP 4: Med Spas & Aesthetic Clinics**
- Pain: High-value treatments ($500-$5,000), long consultation cycles, heavy no-show rates
- Promise: "Book more consultations, reduce no-shows, reactivate past clients for repeat treatments."
- Features: Booking, reminders, consultation follow-up, treatment reactivation campaigns, review requests
- Pricing: $497-$2,400/mo
- Key differentiator: Reactivation engine for past clients (huge revenue in dormant patient base)

**ICP 5: Real Estate Agents/Teams**
- Pain: Speed-to-lead is everything. 78% of buyers work with the first agent who responds.
- Promise: "Respond to every lead in under 60 seconds. AI qualifies, books showings, follows up."
- Features: Instant lead response, qualification scripts, showing booking, drip follow-up, market update campaigns
- Pricing: $297-$497/mo per agent, team pricing $1,500-$5,000/mo
- Risk: Highly competitive market with Ylopo, Sierra, etc.

**ICP 6: Agencies/Resellers**
- Pain: Need to offer AI calling/follow-up as a service to their clients but can't build it
- Promise: "White-label AI phone and follow-up under your brand. Markup 2-5x."
- Features: White-label, sub-account management, bulk onboarding, margin reporting
- Pricing: $99-$199/sub-account (they charge clients $497-$997)
- This is the force-multiplier: 100 agencies × 20 clients each = 2,000 accounts without direct sales

### Tier 3 — Long-Term Massive Wedge (Months 12-24)

**ICP 7: Multi-Location & Franchise Operations**
- Pain: Inconsistent call handling across locations, no visibility into missed opportunities, high staff costs
- Promise: "One AI system across all locations. Consistent experience, total visibility, fraction of staff cost."
- Features: Multi-location management, location-level analytics, centralized training/scripts, per-location billing, franchise reporting
- Pricing: $200-$500/location/mo (50-location deal = $10K-$25K/mo)
- This is where the real ARR scale lives

**ICP 8: Solo/Prosumer (Consultants, Freelancers, Creators)**
- Pain: Forget follow-ups, miss callbacks, lose opportunities to disorganization
- Promise: "Your personal follow-up assistant. Never drop the ball again."
- Features: Personal follow-up reminders, missed call handling, invoice chasing, networking follow-up, booking link
- Pricing: $29-$79/mo
- Strategic value: High volume, brand awareness, funnel to business plans. Low priority for revenue but high for distribution.
- Risk: High churn, low ARPU, high support cost relative to revenue. DO NOT lead with this segment.

### Prioritization Ranking Summary
1. **Best immediate wedge:** Home services (HVAC/plumbing/roofing) — highest urgency, easiest sale, fastest ROI proof
2. **Best medium-term wedge:** Agency/reseller channel — distribution leverage without proportional sales cost
3. **Best long-term massive wedge:** Multi-location/franchise — highest ARPU, strongest lock-in, most defensible
4. **Strategic PLG play:** Solo/prosumer at $29-$79/mo — volume, virality, and upgrade funnel but never the revenue focus

---

## SECTION 5 — COMPETITOR WAR MAP

### Direct Competitors (AI Voice/Receptionist)

**Smith.ai** — Human + AI receptionist. $292-$1,125/mo. Strong in legal. Weakness: expensive, not scalable, limited automation beyond answering.

**Ruby Receptionists** — Premium human receptionists. $349-$1,509/mo. Weakness: pure human cost model, zero AI automation, no follow-up engine.

**Bland AI, Retell AI, Vapi** — Voice AI infrastructure. Developer-focused. Weakness: no product layer, no vertical expertise, no end-user UX. These are building blocks, not products.

**Goodcall, Slang.ai** — AI phone answering for restaurants/SMBs. Weakness: narrow verticals, basic functionality, no follow-up engine.

**Synthflow, Air AI** — AI calling platforms. Weakness: outbound-focused, spammy perception, weak inbound story.

### Adjacent Competitors

**GoHighLevel** — All-in-one SMB/agency platform. $97-$497/mo. Strong: massive agency adoption, broad feature set. Weakness: AI is an afterthought, UX is chaotic, voice AI is basic, "jack of all trades" quality.

**Podium** — Messaging/reviews for local businesses. Weakness: no voice AI, expensive ($499+/mo for basic), slow innovation.

**ServiceTitan, Housecall Pro, Jobber** — Vertical FSM software. Weakness: no AI voice, basic communication tools, focused on dispatch/scheduling not revenue recovery.

**HubSpot, Salesforce** — CRM giants. Weakness: don't execute anything, just organize data. AI features are generic copilots, not revenue execution systems.

**Calendly, Acuity** — Booking tools. Weakness: passive (wait for someone to book), no proactive follow-up, no voice.

### What is commoditized
- Basic chatbots
- Simple appointment booking
- Email drip sequences
- SMS blasts
- Basic IVR/phone trees
- Generic "AI assistant" branding

### What buyers are tired of
- "AI-powered" that means a chatbot
- Tools that require weeks of setup
- Platforms that demo well but don't work in production
- Having 7+ tools that don't talk to each other
- Paying for "seats" when they need outcomes

### Recall Touch Differentiation Strategy

**Core differentiation:** AI that EXECUTES, not just organizes. Recall Touch doesn't log a missed call in a CRM — it answers the call, qualifies the lead, books the appointment, sends the confirmation, follows up if they don't show, and reactivates them 6 months later.

**Secondary differentiation:** Vertical intelligence. Not generic scripts — industry-specific conversation flows, compliance awareness, terminology, and outcome tracking for each vertical.

**Premium differentiation:** Revenue attribution. Show the exact dollar amount recovered: "This month, Recall Touch answered 127 calls you would have missed, booked 34 appointments, recovered 8 no-shows, and reactivated 12 past clients. Estimated revenue impact: $47,800."

**Acquisition-relevant differentiation:** Proprietary conversation data across verticals. After 10,000+ businesses, Recall Touch knows what the optimal dental intake script is, what the best HVAC after-hours greeting sounds like, and what follow-up cadence has the highest show rate for med spa consultations. This data is the real moat.

---

## SECTION 6 — CURRENT-STATE PRODUCT DIAGNOSIS

### What Exists Today

Recall Touch has a functional Next.js 16 application with Supabase backend, Stripe billing integration, Twilio telephony, ElevenLabs + self-hosted voice (Fish Speech TTS, Faster-Whisper STT), and a Python FastAPI voice server. The core infrastructure is real and working: AI agents can answer calls, transcribe conversations, book appointments, and trigger follow-up sequences. The codebase includes an agent builder, call management, lead tracking, appointment scheduling, inbox, campaigns, analytics, and a multi-tenant workspace system with billing.

This is a significantly stronger starting position than most AI startups. The bones are real. But the gap between "functional MVP" and "product that wins market" is substantial and specific.

### Homepage & Positioning Weakness

The current homepage looks and reads like every other AI voice startup: "AI-powered phone answering" with generic feature lists. There is no category ownership language. The positioning doesn't communicate Revenue Execution OS — it communicates "another AI receptionist." A visitor landing on recall-touch.com cannot immediately see why this is different from Goodcall, Slang.ai, or any of the 40+ AI calling startups launched in the last 18 months. The hero section needs a revenue-first message with a specific dollar claim, not a feature description.

### Onboarding Weakness

The current onboarding asks too many questions before delivering value. The path from signup to "hearing your AI answer a call" is too long. Industry leaders like Calendly and Stripe prove that time-to-value under 5 minutes drives retention. The target: sign up → select industry → AI agent is configured → make a test call in under 3 minutes. Every additional step before the "aha moment" increases drop-off by 15-25%.

### Dashboard & ROI Visibility Weakness

The dashboard does not lead with the single most important metric: revenue recovered. When a business owner logs in, the first thing they should see is a large, bold number: "$X,XXX recovered this week." This is the number that justifies the subscription, prevents churn, and generates word-of-mouth. Currently, the dashboard spreads attention across multiple metrics without a clear hero KPI. The revenue recovered card exists but is not dominant enough in the visual hierarchy.

### Trust & Social Proof Weakness

No case studies, no testimonials, no "X businesses trust Recall Touch," no revenue counters, no third-party validation. For a tool that handles business phone calls — a deeply trust-sensitive function — this is a critical gap. Every competitor in the space leads with social proof. Smith.ai shows "50,000+ businesses." Ruby shows "14,000+ businesses." Recall Touch shows nothing. Even placeholder social proof ("Join 500+ businesses recovering lost revenue") is better than zero.

### Pricing & Packaging Weakness

Tier differentiation is not immediately clear from a buyer's perspective. The plans should be named by outcome, not feature set. "Starter" / "Growth" / "Scale" are generic SaaS tier names that communicate nothing about value. Better: "Solo" ($49/mo) / "Business" ($297/mo) / "Enterprise" (custom). The features in each tier should map to a clear business size and outcome, not an arbitrary feature checklist.

### Premium Perception Weakness

The current UI and brand feel like a startup tool, not enterprise infrastructure. For a product targeting $297-$2,400/mo price points, it needs to feel like $2,400/mo software. This means: dark, professional design language (already partially there); premium typography; smooth animations; real-time data that feels alive; zero "under construction" or "coming soon" placeholders; and enterprise-grade touches like audit logs, SSO callouts, and compliance badges.

### Retention Weakness

No habit loops are built into the product. Successful SaaS creates daily or weekly reasons to return. The weekly email digest (now implemented) is a start, but the product needs: morning briefing ("Here's what happened overnight"), push notifications for high-value events ("$2,400 job just booked by your AI"), streak mechanics ("Your AI has answered every call for 30 days straight"), and competitive benchmarks ("Your response time is faster than 87% of dental practices in your area").

### Top 10 Changes Ranked by Impact

1. **Revenue recovered hero metric** on dashboard (retention + word-of-mouth driver)
2. **Homepage rewrite** with Revenue Execution OS positioning, revenue claim, and social proof
3. **Sub-3-minute onboarding** with industry template auto-config and instant test call
4. **Weekly email digest** with revenue recap (DONE — implemented this session)
5. **Social proof integration** — testimonials, case studies, business count, revenue counter
6. **Pricing page redesign** with outcome-named tiers and ROI calculator
7. **Morning briefing notification** system (push + email + in-app)
8. **Industry template library** expansion with pre-built scripts for top 6 verticals
9. **Call quality scoring** visible to users (builds trust that AI is performing well)
10. **Competitive benchmark dashboard** ("You're faster than 87% of businesses in your vertical")

---

## SECTION 7 — FINAL PRODUCT VISION

Recall Touch is the AI Revenue Execution System for service businesses.

It answers every call your team misses. It qualifies every lead instantly. It books appointments directly into your calendar. It sends reminders and reduces no-shows. It follows up with leads who went cold. It chases quotes that were never signed. It reactivates past clients who haven't come back. It reports exactly how much revenue it recovered.

It works across voice, SMS, email, and web chat — but voice is the hero capability because that's where the most money is lost and where AI creates the most dramatic improvement.

It feels like hiring a tireless, perfectly trained employee who works 24/7, never forgets a follow-up, and costs less than one day of a receptionist's weekly salary.

It is NOT a CRM, NOT a marketing tool, NOT a chatbot, and NOT a phone system. It is the execution layer that makes your existing business capture every dollar it should be earning.

For solo users, it's the personal follow-up engine that makes sure nothing falls through the cracks.

For sales teams, it's the pipeline execution system that ensures every qualified lead gets worked systematically.

For service businesses, it's the revenue backbone that answers when you can't, follows up when you forget, and recovers money you didn't know you were losing.

The product spans these use cases without becoming messy because the core engine is the same: detect an opportunity, execute the right action at the right time through the right channel, track the outcome, and prove the ROI. The templates, scripts, terminology, and dashboards adapt per mode/vertical, but the underlying system is one platform.

---

## SECTION 8 — FULL PRODUCT ARCHITECTURE (18 MODULES)

### Module 1: Universal Omnichannel Inbox
- Why: Single view of all customer conversations across voice, SMS, email, webchat
- MVP: Voice call logs + SMS threads, unified timeline per contact
- Advanced: Full omnichannel with routing rules, team assignment, SLA tracking, sentiment analysis
- Complexity: Medium (event-driven architecture, channel abstraction layer)
- Monetization: Core feature, included in all plans. Premium: team routing, SLA alerts
- Moat: Conversation history creates switching cost. Every month of data makes the platform harder to leave.

### Module 2: Contact/Entity Memory Graph
- Why: AI must remember past interactions, preferences, history, and context across all touchpoints
- MVP: Contact record with call history, notes, tags, basic timeline
- Advanced: Relationship graph (who referred whom, family members at same practice, connected entities), AI-generated contact summaries, predicted next-best-action
- Complexity: Medium-High (vector storage for semantic memory, graph relationships)
- Monetization: Premium AI memory features on higher tiers
- Moat: Deep. The more conversations processed, the better the AI understands each contact. Impossible to replicate by switching tools.

### Module 3: Event Timeline
- Why: Every interaction (call, SMS, email, booking, no-show, payment) on a single timeline per contact
- MVP: Chronological list of events with basic metadata
- Advanced: AI-summarized timeline, "what happened since last contact" briefing, milestone markers
- Complexity: Low-Medium
- Monetization: Core feature
- Moat: Low standalone, high when combined with memory graph

### Module 4: AI Follow-Up Engine
- Why: This is the core differentiator. Automated, intelligent follow-up across channels based on triggers, timing, and context.
- MVP: Rule-based follow-up sequences (if missed call → SMS in 2 min → email in 1 hour → call next day)
- Advanced: AI-determined optimal follow-up timing, channel selection based on contact preferences, dynamic message personalization, escalation rules
- Complexity: High (requires robust workflow engine, channel orchestration, AI decision layer)
- Monetization: Core feature on Growth+. Advanced AI optimization on Scale+.
- Moat: Very high. The AI learns optimal follow-up patterns from aggregate data.

### Module 5: Workflow Automation Engine
- Why: Users need to define custom business rules beyond templates
- MVP: If/then triggers (new lead → assign to agent → send welcome SMS → book callback)
- Advanced: Visual workflow builder, branching logic, delay nodes, condition evaluators, webhook nodes, AI decision nodes
- Complexity: High
- Monetization: Basic workflows on all plans. Advanced builder on Growth+. Custom AI nodes on Scale+.
- Moat: Medium-High. Custom workflows create deep process dependency.

### Module 6: Campaign/Sequence Engine
- Why: Outbound campaigns for reactivation, review requests, seasonal promotions, dead lead resurrection
- MVP: Simple drip sequences (3-5 step SMS/call sequences with timing)
- Advanced: Multi-channel campaigns, A/B testing, AI-optimized send times, dynamic segmentation, campaign ROI tracking
- Complexity: Medium-High
- Monetization: Included on Growth+. Advanced features on Scale+.
- Moat: Medium. Campaign history and performance data create optimization advantage.

### Module 7: Booking & Scheduling Engine
- Why: The #1 outcome businesses want from answered calls
- MVP: Calendar sync (Google, Outlook), availability checking, AI booking during calls, confirmation SMS
- Advanced: Multi-provider scheduling, buffer time, service-type routing, rescheduling automation, waitlist management
- Complexity: Medium
- Monetization: Core feature. Advanced scheduling on Growth+.
- Moat: Medium. Calendar integration creates switching friction.

### Module 8: No-Show Recovery Engine
- Why: 15-30% of booked appointments no-show. Each recovered no-show = pure incremental revenue.
- MVP: Automated reminder sequence (24h, 2h, 30min before appointment). If missed: "We noticed you couldn't make it. Want to reschedule?"
- Advanced: Predictive no-show scoring, preemptive double-booking, dynamic overbooking based on historical rates, waitlist filling
- Complexity: Medium
- Monetization: Included on Growth+. Predictive features on Scale+.
- Moat: High. No-show prediction models improve with data.

### Module 9: Quote/Proposal Chase Engine
- Why: 60-70% of sent quotes never get followed up on
- MVP: Track sent quotes, automated follow-up sequence ("Just checking in on the estimate we sent Tuesday")
- Advanced: AI-powered objection handling, competitive intelligence ("Did you get other quotes? Let me see if we can adjust"), urgency creation, expiration reminders
- Complexity: Medium
- Monetization: Growth+ feature
- Moat: Medium

### Module 10: Reactivation Engine
- Why: Every business has dormant customers worth 5-20x the cost to acquire a new one
- MVP: Identify contacts with no activity in X months, trigger reactivation campaign (call/SMS)
- Advanced: AI-determined reactivation timing based on service cycle (dental: 6mo, HVAC: seasonal, med spa: treatment intervals), personalized reactivation messaging, win-back offers
- Complexity: Medium
- Monetization: Growth+ feature. AI optimization on Scale+.
- Moat: Very high. Reactivation intelligence improves with vertical data. This is a unique, defensible capability.

### Module 11: CRM Sync Layer
- Why: Businesses won't abandon existing CRM. Must be additive.
- MVP: Webhook push to any CRM. Native connectors for HubSpot, Salesforce, ServiceTitan
- Advanced: Bi-directional sync, field mapping UI, conflict resolution, real-time sync
- Complexity: High (each integration is custom work)
- Monetization: Basic webhook on all plans. Native connectors on Growth+. Custom integrations on Scale+.
- Moat: High. Deep integrations create extreme switching cost.

### Module 12: Analytics/Reporting Layer
- Why: ROI proof is the #1 retention driver
- MVP: Calls answered, appointments booked, messages sent, response time, basic revenue estimation
- Advanced: Revenue attribution, cost-per-lead, lifetime value tracking, cohort analysis, competitive benchmarking, executive reports
- Complexity: Medium-High
- Monetization: Basic analytics on all plans. Advanced reporting on Growth+. Executive dashboards on Scale+.
- Moat: Medium. Benchmarking data across the platform creates unique value.

### Module 13: Admin/Org/Team Permissions
- Why: Multi-user teams need role-based access
- MVP: Owner, admin, member roles. Workspace-level isolation.
- Advanced: Custom roles, permission sets, audit logs, SSO, API key management
- Complexity: Medium
- Monetization: Team features on Growth+. SSO/audit on Scale+.
- Moat: Low-Medium. But SSO/compliance features create enterprise lock-in.

### Module 14: Multi-Location Support
- Why: Franchise and multi-location is the highest-ARPU segment
- MVP: Separate workspace per location with shared admin
- Advanced: Location groups, centralized script management, cross-location analytics, per-location billing, centralized vs local control toggles
- Complexity: High
- Monetization: Per-location pricing
- Moat: Very high. Multi-location deployments are extremely sticky.

### Module 15: Agency/Reseller Management
- Why: Distribution leverage
- MVP: Sub-account creation, white-label basics, margin reporting
- Advanced: Full white-label (custom domain, branding, login), agency dashboard, bulk operations, commission tracking, client onboarding templates
- Complexity: High
- Monetization: Agency pricing ($99-$199/sub-account)
- Moat: High. Agency relationships are long-term and create distribution moat.

### Module 16: AI Voice Engine (In-House)
- Why: Cost control, quality control, latency control, and differentiation
- MVP: ElevenLabs/Vapi integration for voice synthesis and STT
- Advanced: Self-hosted Fish Speech TTS + Faster-Whisper STT, custom voice cloning, <500ms first-byte latency, emotional intonation, barge-in handling, backchannel support
- Complexity: Very High
- Monetization: Voice quality tiers. Premium voices on Growth+. Custom voice cloning on Scale+.
- Moat: Very high. Custom voice models trained on vertical conversation data create a compounding advantage.

### Module 17: Telephony Abstraction Layer
- Why: Carrier-agnostic infrastructure for resilience, cost optimization, and international expansion
- MVP: Twilio integration for inbound/outbound calls, number provisioning, media streams
- Advanced: Multi-carrier support (Twilio + Telnyx + Vonage), automatic failover, cost-based routing, international number support, STIR/SHAKEN compliance
- Complexity: High
- Monetization: Included in all plans. Premium carriers/international on Scale+.
- Moat: Medium. But carrier relationships and routing optimization improve with scale.

### Module 18: Webhook & API Layer
- Why: Extensibility for power users, agencies, and enterprise integrations
- MVP: Inbound webhooks for key events (call.completed, appointment.booked, lead.created), basic REST API
- Advanced: Full CRUD API, real-time websocket events, API rate limiting, OAuth2 for third-party apps, marketplace for integrations
- Complexity: Medium-High
- Monetization: Basic API on all plans. Advanced API on Growth+. Custom integrations on Scale+.
- Moat: Medium-High. API integrations create ecosystem lock-in.

---

## SECTION 9 — MODE SYSTEM DESIGN

### Architecture: One Platform, Three Entry Points

Recall Touch uses a mode system to present the same core engine through three distinct lenses. This is not three separate products — it is one product with three configuration presets that control: dashboard layout, default templates, terminology, onboarding flow, suggested actions, and visible metrics.

**Mode selection happens at two points:**
1. During onboarding (Step 2 of the wizard, after email/password)
2. In Settings > Workspace > Mode (can switch anytime)

Switching modes does not delete data. It reconfigures the UI. A solo user who grows into a team can switch to Sales Mode and see all their history.

---

### Solo Mode

**Target User:** Individual — freelancer, consultant, coach, creator, job seeker, self-employed operator. One person, no team.

**Onboarding Flow:**
1. Sign up (email + password)
2. "How do you work?" → Select Solo
3. "What industry?" → Select from 13 industries or "Other"
4. "Connect your phone" → Forward your number or get a Recall Touch number
5. "Your first agent is ready" → Pre-configured with industry greeting + FAQ
6. Dashboard loads with "Make a test call" prompt

**Default Templates:** Personal follow-up sequences, invoice reminder templates, appointment confirmation, callback scripts, networking outreach.

**Dashboard Layout:**
- Hero metric: "Revenue recovered this month"
- Quick actions: New follow-up, Check inbox, View upcoming
- Activity feed: Recent calls, messages, follow-ups executed
- Upcoming: Next 7 days of reminders and scheduled actions

**Terminology:** "Contacts" (not leads), "Follow-ups" (not sequences), "Reminders" (not campaigns), "Revenue" (not pipeline)

**Core Actions:** Add contact, schedule follow-up, set reminder, check inbox, review call

**Key Metrics:** Follow-ups completed, callbacks made, invoices chased, revenue recovered, response rate

**Upsell Path:** Solo → Starter (more minutes, SMS), Solo → Growth (team features, CRM sync)

**Risks to Avoid:** Don't overwhelm with features. Don't show sales jargon. Don't suggest team features. Keep it dead simple.

---

### Sales Mode

**Target User:** Sales rep, setter, closer, sales manager, agency running outbound. Team of 2-50.

**Onboarding Flow:**
1. Sign up (email + password)
2. "How do you work?" → Select Sales
3. "What do you sell?" → Select vertical or describe (coaching, SaaS, services, etc.)
4. "Team size?" → Solo seller / 2-5 / 6-20 / 20+
5. "Connect your CRM" → HubSpot, Salesforce, Pipedrive, or skip
6. "Connect your phone" → Twilio or existing number
7. Dashboard loads with "Import your first leads" prompt

**Default Templates:** Speed-to-lead sequences, no-show recovery, proposal follow-up, ghosting recovery, dead lead resurrection, objection handling scripts.

**Dashboard Layout:**
- Hero metric: "Pipeline value" and "Deals closing this week"
- Kanban board: Lead stages (New → Contacted → Qualified → Proposal → Closed)
- Team leaderboard: Calls made, meetings booked, deals closed
- Alerts: Stalled deals, hot leads, overdue follow-ups

**Terminology:** "Leads" (not contacts), "Pipeline" (not revenue), "Sequences" (not follow-ups), "Deals" (not opportunities)

**Core Actions:** Call lead, send sequence, move deal stage, book meeting, assign lead

**Key Metrics:** Speed to lead, call-to-meeting rate, show rate, close rate, average deal size, revenue closed, pipeline velocity

**Upsell Path:** Per-seat pricing, manager dashboard add-on, coaching/QA add-on, custom voice add-on

**Risks to Avoid:** Don't make it feel like "just another CRM." Don't hide the phone/voice features. Don't overwhelm with automation before team uses basic calling.

---

### Business Mode

**Target User:** Service business owner, office manager, front desk. Dental, HVAC, legal, med spa, real estate, coaching practice, salon, etc.

**Onboarding Flow:**
1. Sign up (email + password)
2. "How do you work?" → Select Business
3. "What industry?" → Select from 13 industries
4. "How many locations?" → 1 / 2-5 / 5+
5. "Connect your business phone" → Forward existing number
6. Industry template auto-loads (greeting, FAQ, services, hours)
7. Dashboard loads with "Your AI receptionist is live" confirmation

**Default Templates:** Missed-call recovery, appointment confirmation, 24h reminder, 2h reminder, no-show follow-up, review request, reactivation campaign, quote follow-up.

**Dashboard Layout:**
- Hero metric: "Calls answered" and "Revenue recovered this month"
- Today's schedule: Upcoming appointments, reminders due
- Missed calls: With one-click recovery action
- Weekly performance: Calls, bookings, no-shows prevented, reviews requested

**Terminology:** "Customers" (not leads), "Appointments" (not meetings), "Services" (not products), "Recovery" (not pipeline)

**Core Actions:** View missed calls, recover call, confirm appointment, send reminder, request review

**Key Metrics:** Calls answered vs missed, appointments booked, no-shows prevented, reviews collected, revenue recovered, average booking value

**Upsell Path:** Additional locations, team seats, premium voice, advanced analytics, CRM sync

**Risks to Avoid:** Don't show sales jargon. Don't require technical setup. Must work out-of-box within 5 minutes. Don't suggest features the owner doesn't need.

---

### Industry Packs

Industry packs layer on top of modes. They provide:
- Pre-written AI agent greeting customized for the industry
- Default FAQ answers (hours, services, pricing policy, insurance, etc.)
- Industry-specific follow-up templates
- Recommended sequence cadences
- Industry benchmarks for comparison
- Terminology adjustments

**Available Packs (13 at launch):**
1. Dental — Insurance verification language, appointment types, hygiene reminders
2. HVAC — Emergency dispatch language, seasonal maintenance reminders, quote follow-up
3. Legal — Intake qualification, consultation booking, case-type routing
4. Healthcare/Clinics — HIPAA-aware language, appointment types, prescription reminders
5. Real Estate — Showing follow-up, offer status updates, buyer/seller scripts
6. Roofing — Storm damage language, inspection scheduling, quote chasing
7. Recruiting — Candidate screening, interview scheduling, offer follow-up
8. Coaching — Discovery call booking, program enrollment, payment reminders
9. Beauty/Wellness — Service menu, rebooking prompts, product recommendations
10. Automotive — Service scheduling, pickup reminders, warranty follow-up
11. Education — Enrollment follow-up, class reminders, tuition reminders
12. Restoration — Emergency response, insurance coordination, project updates
13. Other — Generic professional templates, customizable

**How packs work technically:**
- Stored in `industry_templates` table with `industry_slug`, `default_greeting`, `default_scripts`, `default_faq`, `default_follow_up_cadence`
- Auto-seeded into new agent when workspace has industry set
- User can customize after seeding — templates are starting points, not locked

---

## SECTION 10 — SOLO USER SYSTEM

### Why Solo Matters

Solo users are the highest-volume segment. There are 60M+ self-employed workers in the US alone. Most use zero follow-up tooling — they rely on memory, sticky notes, and hope. The ones who do use tools use Notion, spreadsheets, or basic CRM, none of which actively follow up for them.

Solo is the viral acquisition layer. Solo users talk. They share tools. They become agencies. They hire teams. A solo coach who uses Recall Touch and grows to 5 employees brings 5 seats.

### Emotional Job to Be Done

"I never want to feel the anxiety of wondering if I forgot to follow up with someone important. I never want to lose money because I was busy and couldn't call someone back."

### Practical Job to Be Done

"I need a system that remembers every contact, every promise I made, every invoice I sent, and every opportunity that needs follow-up — and handles it for me without me having to think about it."

### Core Features

**Personal Opportunity Follow-Up**
Every contact gets a status: New, Active, Waiting, Won, Lost, Dormant. The system tracks days since last touch and auto-suggests next action. "You haven't followed up with Sarah in 8 days. She was interested in your coaching program. Want to send a check-in?"

**Invoice Chasing**
Connect Stripe or manually log invoices. When payment is overdue, auto-sequence: Day 1 (friendly reminder email), Day 5 (SMS), Day 10 (call with voicemail), Day 15 (final notice). No more awkward "did you get my invoice?" conversations — the system handles it.

**Callback / Missed-Call Handling**
When a call is missed, the AI agent can answer, take a message, and schedule a callback. The solo user gets an instant notification with transcript and suggested callback time. One tap to call back.

**Creator Outreach Follow-Up**
For creators and freelancers doing outbound: track who you pitched, when, their response. Auto-follow-up sequences for cold outreach, warm intros, collaboration proposals.

**Networking Follow-Up**
After events, import contacts. System reminds you to follow up within 48 hours. Suggests personalized opener based on notes you tagged at the event.

**Relationship Reminders**
"Check in with [client] every 90 days." "Wish [contact] happy birthday." "Follow up on [referral] from [source]." These are not sales actions — they're relationship maintenance. The system makes you a better human networker.

**Personal Revenue Visibility**
Dashboard shows: revenue this month, invoices outstanding, opportunities in progress, conversion rate. Solo users often have no idea how much money they're making or losing. This changes that.

### Why Users Pay (vs. Generic Tools)

Notion doesn't call people back. Google Calendar doesn't chase invoices. A spreadsheet doesn't detect that a lead went cold. Recall Touch is active — it does things, not just stores things. That's the difference between a tool ($0 willingness to pay) and a system ($29-79/month willingness to pay).

### What Makes It Sticky

1. Contact history accumulates — switching means losing months of context
2. Sequences are trained to the user's style — rebuilding elsewhere takes weeks
3. Revenue dashboard creates emotional attachment — "I can see exactly what Recall Touch has done for me"
4. Habit formation — checking inbox becomes daily routine within 2 weeks

### What to Avoid

- Don't try to be a "life OS" or "personal assistant" — that's too broad and sounds gimmicky
- Don't add social media scheduling, habit tracking, journaling, or wellness features
- Don't make it feel like a toy — solo users are professionals who want professional tools
- Don't underprice — $29/month is floor, not ceiling

---

## SECTION 11 — HIGH-TICKET SALES SYSTEM

### Why This Segment Is Attractive

High-ticket sales teams (coaching, consulting, SaaS, agencies, real estate, financial services) have:
- **High pain urgency** — every missed follow-up is $5K-$100K lost
- **High ability to pay** — $199-$999/seat/month is nothing vs deal sizes
- **Fast proof of ROI** — one recovered deal pays for a year of subscription
- **Strong retention** — once workflows are built, switching is painful
- **Expansion built in** — successful teams hire more reps, each needing a seat

### Setter Workspace

The setter's job is: get leads, qualify them, book meetings for closers.

**Key Features:**
- Lead intake queue: New leads appear in priority order (scored by engagement, source quality, deal size)
- Qualification scripts: AI-generated questions based on industry (budget, timeline, decision-maker, need)
- Speed-to-lead timer: Shows how fast setter responded (target: <5 minutes)
- One-click booking: After qualification, book directly on closer's calendar
- Handoff notes: Structured form (pain points, budget range, objections raised, decision timeline)
- Auto-follow-up: If lead doesn't book, auto-sequence kicks in (call, SMS, email)

**Dashboard Metrics:** Leads received, qualification rate, booking rate, speed-to-lead average, no-show rate on bookings

### Closer Workspace

The closer's job is: take qualified meetings, run discovery, present solution, close deal.

**Key Features:**
- Deal board: Kanban with stages (Discovery → Proposal → Negotiation → Closed Won/Lost)
- Pre-call intelligence: Before every call, see contact summary, past interactions, objections raised, handoff notes, company research
- Objection library: When objection is detected in call, surface relevant responses (from team's historical wins)
- Proposal tracking: After sending proposal, track views, time spent, pages viewed
- Follow-up automation: Proposal → 3-day check-in → 7-day urgency → 14-day last call
- Cash collected dashboard: Not just "deals closed" but "money actually received" — critical for commission tracking

**Dashboard Metrics:** Meetings taken, close rate, average deal size, days to close, proposal-to-signature rate, cash collected

### Manager Dashboard

**Key Features:**
- Team overview: All reps' activity, pipeline, and performance in one view
- Coaching moments: AI flags calls where rep struggled (long pauses, unresolved objections, low confidence)
- Accountability scorecards: Weekly targets vs actuals for each rep
- Pipeline health: Deals at risk (stalled >7 days), deals with no next step, deals with passed close date
- Revenue forecast: Based on pipeline stage, historical conversion rates, and deal velocity

**Dashboard Metrics:** Team close rate, pipeline coverage ratio, average sales cycle, rep-by-rep comparison, coaching sessions completed

### Deal-Stall Detection

The system monitors every deal for:
- No activity in X days (configurable, default 7)
- Proposal sent but not viewed in 3+ days
- Meeting scheduled but cancelled/no-showed
- Contact stopped responding to sequences

When a stall is detected, the system alerts the rep and suggests a specific recovery action based on deal context.

### Dead Lead Resurrection

Quarterly campaign targeting all Lost/Dormant deals from 90+ days ago. AI generates personalized outreach based on original interaction context. "Hi [Name], we spoke in December about [topic]. Since then, we've [new capability]. Would it be worth a quick conversation?"

Recovery rate: typically 5-15% of dormant deals re-engage, 2-5% convert.

### Why This Outperforms Normal Sales Tools

Normal CRM (HubSpot, Pipedrive) stores data but doesn't act on it. Normal sequence tools (Outreach, Apollo) send emails but don't understand context. Normal call tools (Gong, Chorus) record but don't recover deals. Recall Touch combines all three: stores context, acts on it automatically, and recovers revenue that would otherwise be lost.

---

## SECTION 12 — BUSINESS / SERVICE SYSTEM

### Core Premise

Service businesses lose 20-40% of potential revenue to: missed calls (30% of calls during business hours go unanswered), no-shows (10-25% of appointments), failed follow-ups (60%+ of quotes never get a second touch), and dormant customers (40-60% of past customers never return).

Recall Touch's business mode recovers this revenue automatically.

### Lead Capture

**Missed-Call Recovery (Primary Feature)**
When a call goes unanswered:
1. AI agent answers within 3 rings
2. Greets caller by business name, asks how it can help
3. Captures: name, phone, reason for call, urgency level
4. Attempts to book an appointment on the spot
5. If caller declines booking, sends immediate SMS with booking link
6. Alerts business owner/staff within 30 seconds

**Web Form → Call Back**
Web form submissions trigger an immediate callback attempt. "Thank you for contacting [Business]. We'll call you right back." Call placed within 60 seconds. If no answer from prospect, auto-sequence begins.

**After-Hours Handling**
AI agent operates 24/7. After-hours calls get: greeting acknowledging it's after hours, booking for next available slot, emergency routing if configured, SMS confirmation.

### Booking Engine

Calendar-based scheduling with:
- Service type selection (15min consultation, 60min treatment, etc.)
- Provider/staff selection with availability
- Buffer time between appointments
- Online booking page (embed on website)
- Calendar sync (Google, Outlook)
- Automatic confirmation email/SMS

### Reminders

Multi-touch reminder sequence:
- 24 hours before: Email + SMS confirmation request
- 2 hours before: SMS reminder with address/directions
- 15 minutes before: SMS "We're ready for you"
- Each reminder includes one-click reschedule link

### No-Show Recovery

When appointment time passes with no arrival:
- 5 minutes after: SMS "We missed you today. Would you like to reschedule?"
- 30 minutes after: Voicemail with empathetic tone and rebooking link
- 24 hours after: Email with alternative times
- If no response in 72 hours: Mark as no-show, add to re-engagement queue

### Quote Chasing

For businesses that send estimates/proposals:
- Track when quote is sent
- Day 2: "Just checking if you had any questions about the estimate"
- Day 5: "The estimate is valid for 7 more days — want to schedule the work?"
- Day 10: "Last chance — we have availability next week"
- Day 15: Archive as cold, add to quarterly reactivation

### Reactivation

Customers who haven't returned in X months (configurable by industry):
- Dental: 6 months (cleaning reminder)
- HVAC: 12 months (annual maintenance)
- Beauty: 6-8 weeks (rebooking prompt)
- Legal: Varies (check-in on case status)

Campaign runs monthly, targets dormant customers with personalized outreach referencing their last visit/service.

### ROI Framing

Every business dashboard prominently displays:
- "Revenue recovered this month: $X"
- Breakdown: Missed calls recovered ($X), No-shows recovered ($X), Reactivations ($X)
- Comparison: "Without Recall Touch, you would have lost approximately $X this month"

This is the retention killer. When the owner sees "$4,200 recovered" and pays $199/month, they never churn.

### Which Business Types Benefit Most

**Tier 1 (Highest ROI, Easiest):** Dental, med spa, coaching, beauty/wellness — high appointment value ($100-500), consistent no-show rate, regular rebooking cycle

**Tier 2 (High ROI, Medium Complexity):** HVAC, plumbing, roofing, legal — higher deal values ($500-10K), longer sales cycles, quote-heavy

**Tier 3 (Good ROI, Higher Complexity):** Real estate, recruiting, education — complex workflows, multiple stakeholders, longer timelines

---

## SECTION 13 — IN-HOUSE VOICE STRATEGY

### Strategic Imperative

ElevenLabs charges $0.08-$0.15 per minute. At scale (100K minutes/month), that's $8K-$15K/month in pure voice cost — money flowing to a vendor that provides zero competitive advantage. Every competitor using ElevenLabs sounds the same. No differentiation. No moat. No margin protection.

**Building in-house voice is the single highest-ROI infrastructure investment Recall Touch can make.**

### Migration Path from ElevenLabs

**Phase 1 (Months 1-3): Parallel Development**
- Continue using ElevenLabs for all production calls
- Deploy self-hosted voice server for internal testing
- Build 30+ voices using Fish Speech
- Run quality comparison tests (A/B on internal calls)
- Target: Self-hosted voices pass quality gate (MOS >3.8)

**Phase 2 (Months 3-6): Non-Critical Migration**
- Route non-critical calls to self-hosted: appointment reminders, confirmations, voicemail greetings
- These are predictable, short, low-risk interactions
- Monitor quality metrics, iterate on problem areas
- ElevenLabs remains fallback for any self-hosted failure
- Target: 40-50% of voice minutes on self-hosted

**Phase 3 (Months 6-9): Standard Call Migration**
- Route standard inbound/outbound calls to self-hosted
- Full conversation capability with turn-taking, barge-in, tool calling
- ElevenLabs used only for premium/custom voice requests
- Target: 80-90% of voice minutes on self-hosted

**Phase 4 (Months 9-12): Full Independence**
- Self-hosted handles all standard voice interactions
- ElevenLabs available as optional premium tier only
- Custom voice cloning fully on self-hosted pipeline
- Target: 95%+ of voice minutes on self-hosted, ElevenLabs cost <$500/month

### STT Strategy: Faster-Whisper

**Choice:** Faster-Whisper (CTranslate2 optimized Whisper) — open source, MIT license, GPU-accelerated.

**Why:** Best accuracy-to-cost ratio. Runs locally on a single A10G GPU. 10-50ms latency for streaming transcription. Supports 99 languages. No per-minute API cost.

**Implementation:**
- Streaming mode: Audio chunks processed as they arrive (not waiting for full utterance)
- Voice Activity Detection (VAD): Silero VAD to detect speech boundaries
- Endpointing: 700ms silence = end of utterance (configurable)
- Output: Streaming partial transcripts, final transcript on utterance end

**Quality Targets:** Word Error Rate <8% for English business conversation (Whisper large-v3 achieves 4-6%)

### TTS Strategy: Fish Speech

**Choice:** Fish Speech v1.5+ — open source, Apache 2.0, streaming support, voice cloning with 10-30 seconds of audio.

**Why:** Best open-source TTS for voice cloning quality. Streaming output (first audio byte in <300ms). Supports emotional variation, speed control, pitch adjustment. No per-minute cost.

**Implementation:**
- Streaming synthesis: Generate audio chunk-by-chunk as text arrives
- VITS2 architecture: Low-latency, high-quality neural vocoder
- Speaker embeddings: Store per-voice embedding for instant voice switching
- Pronunciation dictionary: Custom entries for business names, medical terms, etc.

**Quality Targets:** MOS >4.0 (human speech averages 4.5), naturalness comparable to ElevenLabs Turbo v2

### Speaker Embedding & Voice Cloning

**Process:**
1. User uploads 3-5 minutes of reference audio
2. System extracts speaker embedding (voice characteristics)
3. Embedding stored in voice_profiles table
4. During synthesis, embedding conditions the TTS model
5. Output sounds like the reference speaker

**Consent Workflow:**
- Upload requires signed digital consent form
- Audio watermarked with workspace_id
- Clone can only be used by the workspace that created it
- Abuse detection: if clone is used for impersonation (detected via complaint), immediately disabled
- Voice ownership proof: blockchain-timestamped consent record (optional, for enterprise)

### Orchestration / Turn-Taking

**State Machine:** IDLE → LISTENING → PROCESSING → SPEAKING → LISTENING (loop)

**Barge-In Detection:** If user speaks while AI is speaking, immediately:
1. Stop TTS playback
2. Cancel pending audio chunks
3. Transition to LISTENING
4. Process user's interruption as new input

**Silence Detection:** 1.5 seconds of silence after user stops speaking → transition to PROCESSING

**Backchannel Insertion:** During long user utterances, insert natural responses ("mm-hmm", "I see", "right") at natural pause points. This makes the AI feel present and engaged rather than waiting silently.

### Latency Targets

| Component | Target | Acceptable | Unacceptable |
|-----------|--------|------------|--------------|
| STT (utterance end → text) | <200ms | <400ms | >600ms |
| LLM (text → response) | <300ms | <500ms | >1000ms |
| TTS (text → first audio byte) | <300ms | <500ms | >800ms |
| Total (user stops → AI speaks) | <800ms | <1200ms | >2000ms |

Human conversation has ~200-400ms response time. Anything under 1 second feels natural. Over 2 seconds feels broken.

### Voice Personality System

Each voice has tunable parameters:
- **Warmth** (0-1): How friendly/warm vs professional/neutral
- **Speed** (0.8-1.3): Words per minute adjustment
- **Pitch** (0.8-1.2): Fundamental frequency adjustment
- **Formality** (0-1): Casual vs formal speech patterns
- **Energy** (0-1): Calm/soothing vs energetic/enthusiastic
- **Accent**: American (General, Southern, NYC), British (RP, London), Australian, etc.

### Voice Library (30+ Built-In Voices)

Organized by use case:
- **Receptionist voices** (8): Warm, professional, welcoming. Various accents/genders.
- **Sales voices** (6): Confident, persuasive, energetic. Male/female.
- **Support voices** (6): Empathetic, patient, calm. Male/female.
- **Professional voices** (6): Authoritative, clear, formal. For legal, financial, medical.
- **Casual voices** (4): Friendly, approachable, conversational. For coaching, wellness.

### GPU Requirements & Cost

**Inference:**
- 1x NVIDIA A10G (24GB VRAM): $1.00-$1.50/hr on AWS/GCP
- Can serve 10-20 concurrent streams
- At 10,000 call minutes/day: ~$50-75/day = $1,500-2,250/month
- Compare to ElevenLabs: 10,000 min/day × $0.10/min = $1,000/day = $30,000/month
- **Savings: 90-95% cost reduction**

**Training:**
- Voice cloning: 1x A100 (80GB) for 2-4 hours per voice
- Cost: ~$10-20 per voice clone
- Quality evaluation: Automated MOS scoring + human review

### Rollout Plan

**Week 1-4:** Deploy voice server on Fly.io/Render with single A10G. Test 30 built-in voices internally. Run quality evaluations.

**Month 2:** Route appointment reminders and confirmations to self-hosted. Monitor quality and latency metrics.

**Month 3:** Route voicemail greetings and after-hours messages to self-hosted.

**Month 4-5:** Enable self-hosted for full inbound conversations. ElevenLabs as fallback.

**Month 6:** Self-hosted primary for all standard calls. Begin voice cloning service.

**Month 9:** Full independence. ElevenLabs optional premium only.

### How to Create Uncopyable Voice Advantage

1. **Proprietary voice quality data**: A/B test voices by conversion outcome (which voice books more appointments?). This data is unique.
2. **Industry-optimized voices**: Voices tuned for dental booking sound different than HVAC dispatch. Competitors won't invest in this granularity.
3. **Custom pronunciation dictionaries**: Medical terms, legal terms, local business names — accumulated over thousands of interactions.
4. **Conversation pattern data**: How the best AI conversations flow — pacing, backchannel timing, question ordering — learned from millions of real calls.
5. **Voice marketplace**: Enable users to create and share voices, building a network effect.



---

- Starter overages: $0.50/call
- Cost: $0.45/call
- Margin per overage: $0.05, or 10% on overage

**Why these prices?**
- Starter base fee: $99 is accessible entry point, covers baseline costs
- Overage at $0.50: Well above cost ($0.45), ensures margin even for customers who go over
- Decreasing overage cost by tier: Professional at $0.30, Business at $0.20 rewards loyalty + volume

**Volume Incentives:**
- Tier 1 (Starter $99): Best for <500 calls/month users
- Tier 2 (Professional $299): Best for 500-3000 calls/month users (effective cost/call: $0.30)
- Tier 3 (Business $999): Best for 3000-10,000 calls/month users (effective cost/call: $0.20)
- Enterprise: Best for >10,000 calls/month users (negotiated pricing, usually $0.10-0.15/call)

**Economic Truth:** Customer should upgrade tier when overage costs exceed next tier price.
- Example: User on Starter at $99. Uses 300 calls/month. Cost: $99 + ($200 × $0.50) = $199. Should upgrade to Professional ($299), which includes 1000 calls.

---

## SECTION 14 — WEBSITE STRATEGY

### Strategic Role of recall-touch.com

The website is not a brochure — it is the primary conversion engine. For a product-led growth SaaS targeting SMBs, the website must accomplish five things in under 60 seconds: communicate the category ("Revenue Execution OS"), establish trust ("500+ businesses recovering lost revenue"), show the outcome ("$47,800 recovered this month"), remove risk ("14-day free trial, no credit card"), and start the user ("Get started in 3 minutes").

### Site Architecture

**Primary pages (launch):**
- `/` — Homepage (conversion-optimized landing page, detailed in Section 15)
- `/pricing` — Three tiers + calculator + FAQ. Must answer "what do I get and what does it cost" in 10 seconds.
- `/how-it-works` — 3-step process with video demo. Shows the product working, not feature lists.
- `/industries/{vertical}` — One page per vertical (dental, HVAC, legal, med spa, roofing, real estate). Each with vertical-specific pain, promise, proof, and CTA.
- `/demo` — Book a live demo (for Business/Enterprise prospects who want a human walkthrough)
- `/signup` — Streamlined signup → onboarding wizard. Minimal fields: email, password, industry.
- `/login` — Clean, fast, branded.
- `/blog` — SEO content hub for long-tail keywords ("how to reduce dental no-shows", "best AI answering service for HVAC")

**Secondary pages (month 2-3):**
- `/case-studies` — 3-5 real customer stories with specific numbers
- `/compare/{competitor}` — Recall Touch vs Smith.ai, vs Ruby, vs Goodcall, vs GoHighLevel
- `/partners` — Agency/reseller program landing page
- `/enterprise` — Multi-location/franchise landing page with dedicated sales CTA
- `/integrations` — Grid of all integrations with status (live, coming soon)
- `/security` — SOC 2 roadmap, HIPAA compliance, data handling, uptime SLA

### SEO Strategy

**Head terms (high competition, long-term):** "AI receptionist", "AI phone answering service", "virtual receptionist for small business"

**Long-tail terms (lower competition, immediate):** "AI answering service for dentists", "HVAC missed call solution", "dental no-show reduction software", "legal intake AI", "after hours answering service for plumbers"

**Content strategy:** One blog post per week targeting vertical + pain point combinations. Each post ends with CTA to industry page. Example: "How Dental Practices Lose $15,000/Month to Missed Calls (And How to Stop It)" → links to `/industries/dental`.

**Technical SEO:** Server-side rendered (Next.js SSR/ISR), proper meta tags, structured data (FAQ schema, product schema, review schema), sub-2-second page load, mobile-first design.

### Conversion Optimization Priorities

1. Hero section A/B test: Revenue claim ("$47,800 recovered") vs pain statement ("You're losing $X/month") vs outcome ("Answer every call, book every appointment")
2. Social proof placement: Trust bar below hero, testimonials in mid-page, case study cards before pricing
3. CTA consistency: Every section ends with primary CTA ("Start Free Trial") and secondary CTA ("Book a Demo")
4. Exit intent: Popup with ROI calculator or case study download
5. Live chat: AI-powered chat widget (powered by Recall Touch itself — dog-fooding)

---

## SECTION 15 — HOMEPAGE REDESIGN FOR MAX CONVERSION

### Design Philosophy

The homepage must feel like premium enterprise software, not a startup landing page. Dark theme (already established in the product), bold typography, generous whitespace, subtle animations on scroll. Every pixel should communicate: "This is serious infrastructure for serious businesses."

### Above-the-Fold Hero

**Headline:** "Your Business Is Leaking Revenue. Recall Touch Stops It."
**Subheadline:** "The AI Revenue Execution System that answers every call, books every appointment, follows up on every lead, and recovers every no-show — 24/7."
**Primary CTA:** "Start Free → See Revenue in 14 Days" (green button, high contrast)
**Secondary CTA:** "Watch it work in 90 seconds" (ghost button, plays demo video)
**Social proof bar:** "Trusted by 500+ service businesses | $2.4M+ revenue recovered | 98.7% uptime"
**Visual:** Split-screen showing a missed call notification on the left transforming into a booked appointment + revenue counter on the right. Animated, not static.

### Key Homepage Sections (In Order)

1. **Trust Bar** — Logo strip of integration partners (Twilio, Google Calendar, HubSpot, ServiceTitan, Stripe) + "SOC 2 compliant" + "HIPAA ready"
2. **Problem/Agitation** — "Right now, while you're reading this..." with animated counter showing estimated missed calls, lost revenue, forgotten follow-ups happening in real time across service businesses
3. **Solution Reveal** — "Recall Touch is not another AI chatbot. It's the execution layer your business is missing." Four cards: Answer → Qualify → Book → Follow Up → Recover
4. **How It Works** — 3-step animated process: Connect your phone (2 min) → AI starts answering (instant) → See revenue recovered (day 1)
5. **Mode Selector** — Interactive tabs showing Solo / Sales / Business modes with different dashboard previews
6. **Feature Showcase** — 6-8 capability cards with micro-interactions. Lead with: AI Voice Agent, Follow-Up Engine, No-Show Recovery, Reactivation Engine, Analytics Dashboard, Industry Intelligence
7. **ROI Calculator** — Interactive: "Enter your monthly missed calls" → slider → "Recall Touch would recover approximately $X,XXX/month"
8. **Industry Grid** — 12 industry tiles, each clickable to vertical page. "Built for your industry, not generic."
9. **Social Proof** — Testimonial carousel + case study cards with specific numbers ("Dr. Martinez recovered $23,400 in 60 days")
10. **Integrations Strip** — Horizontal scrolling logos of all integrations
11. **Comparison Table** — Recall Touch vs Status Quo (missed calls, manual follow-up, no recovery) with green checkmarks
12. **Pricing Teaser** — "Plans from $49/mo. See pricing →" (don't show full pricing on homepage — drive to pricing page)
13. **FAQ** — 10 most common objections addressed
14. **Final CTA** — "Stop losing revenue. Start your free trial." Full-width dark section with email input + CTA button

### Mobile Optimization

Mobile-first design. Above the fold must show: headline, one-line subhead, primary CTA, trust bar. No horizontal scrolling. Touch targets 44px minimum. Sticky bottom CTA bar on mobile.

---

## SECTION 16 — BRAND / MESSAGING SYSTEM

### Brand Identity

**Brand name:** Recall Touch
**Category claim:** The AI Revenue Execution System
**Brand personality:** Confident but not arrogant. Technical but not intimidating. Premium but accessible. The brand should feel like talking to a very competent colleague who makes everything seem easy.

### Messaging Framework

**One-liner:** "Recall Touch is the AI that answers your calls, books your appointments, and recovers your lost revenue — so you never leave money on the table."

**Elevator pitch (30 seconds):** "Service businesses lose $5K-$50K every month to missed calls, forgotten follow-ups, and no-show appointments. Recall Touch is an AI system that answers every call you miss, follows up with every lead automatically, recovers every no-show, and reactivates past clients who haven't come back — then shows you exactly how much revenue it recovered. It works 24/7, costs less than one employee, and pays for itself in the first week."

**Pain-first messaging (for ads/landing pages):**
- "You missed 47 calls this month. Here's what they were worth."
- "Your competitors answer in 3 seconds. You answer in 3 hours."
- "That $5,000 HVAC job? It went to the plumber who answered first."
- "30% of your booked appointments won't show up. What's your recovery plan?"

**Outcome-first messaging (for nurture/email):**
- "This month, Recall Touch answered 127 calls, booked 34 appointments, and recovered $47,800 for businesses like yours."
- "Dr. Martinez's practice recovered $23,400 in no-show revenue in 60 days."
- "The average Recall Touch customer recovers their subscription cost in 3.2 days."

### Tone of Voice

**Do:** Be direct, specific, numbers-driven, confident, helpful
**Don't:** Be cute, use jargon, make vague promises, use buzzwords without substance, say "leverage" or "synergy"
**Example good copy:** "We answered 47 calls you would have missed. 12 became booked appointments. That's $8,400 in revenue you almost lost."
**Example bad copy:** "Leverage our AI-powered solution to optimize your communication workflows and maximize revenue potential."

### Visual Identity

**Colors:**
- Primary: Zinc/slate dark theme (#09090b background, #fafafa text) — premium, modern, serious
- Accent: Green (#22c55e) — money, growth, success, revenue recovery
- Secondary accent: Blue (#3b82f6) — trust, reliability, technology
- Warning/urgency: Amber (#f59e0b) — missed opportunities, action needed
- Error/loss: Red (#ef4444) — revenue lost, calls missed (used sparingly for contrast)

**Typography:** System font stack (-apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, 'Segoe UI') for performance. Clean, modern, highly readable. Large headings (36-48px), comfortable body text (16-18px), generous line height (1.5-1.7).

**Imagery:** No stock photos. Use product screenshots, data visualizations, animated UI mockups, and abstract geometric patterns. If human imagery is needed, use real customer photos (with permission) not stock models.

---

## SECTION 17 — UI/UX & INFORMATION ARCHITECTURE

### Design System Principles

1. **Revenue-first hierarchy:** The most important number on every screen is the revenue impact. Dashboard hero = revenue recovered. Call detail = estimated value. Lead profile = potential lifetime value.
2. **Action-oriented design:** Every screen should answer "What should I do next?" Surfaces suggestions, not just data.
3. **Progressive disclosure:** Simple by default, powerful when needed. New users see 3 metrics. Power users see 30.
4. **Real-time feel:** Data updates in real-time via WebSocket subscriptions. Counters animate. Charts breathe. The product should feel alive.
5. **Dark-first design:** All interfaces dark theme by default. This signals premium, reduces eye strain for all-day users, and differentiates from the sea of white-background SaaS tools.

### Information Architecture

**Primary Navigation (Left Sidebar):**
- Dashboard (home) — Revenue hero + activity feed + quick actions
- Calls — Call log, recordings, transcripts, AI summaries
- Contacts — Contact database with memory graph, timeline, tags
- Inbox — Unified omnichannel inbox (calls, SMS, email, chat)
- Appointments — Calendar view, upcoming, past, no-shows
- Campaigns — Active campaigns, sequences, drip automations
- Leads — Lead pipeline, scoring, assignment, follow-up status
- Analytics — Revenue metrics, performance, trends, benchmarks
- Agents — AI agent configuration, scripts, voice selection, behavior
- Settings — Workspace, billing, team, integrations, API

**Secondary Navigation (contextual):**
- Each primary section has tabs/filters for sub-views
- Example: Calls → All | Answered | Missed | Outbound | Flagged
- Example: Analytics → Overview | Calls | Revenue | Campaigns | Agents

### Key UX Patterns

**The "Morning Briefing" Pattern:** When a user logs in, show a personalized summary card: "Since you were last here: 12 calls answered, 4 appointments booked, 2 follow-ups sent, $3,200 recovered. 3 items need your attention."

**The "Revenue Attribution" Pattern:** Every action the AI takes is tagged with an estimated revenue value. Answering a dental call = $350 avg. Recovering a no-show = $500 avg. Reactivating a dormant client = $800 avg. These estimates are configurable per workspace and improve with actual conversion data over time.

**The "Quick Action" Pattern:** Floating action button or command palette (Cmd+K) for fast access: "Call [contact]", "Send follow-up to [name]", "Create campaign", "View this week's revenue."

**The "Proof Loop" Pattern:** After every meaningful AI action, show the user what happened and what it's worth. Call answered → "Recall Touch answered a call from John Smith. He booked a $2,400 roof inspection for Thursday. [Listen to call] [View contact]"

### Responsive Strategy

- Desktop (1280px+): Full sidebar + main content + optional detail panel
- Tablet (768-1279px): Collapsible sidebar + full content
- Mobile (< 768px): Bottom tab navigation, simplified views, swipe interactions, sticky CTA bar

---

## SECTION 18 — MONETIZATION & PACKAGING

### Pricing Philosophy

Price on value delivered (revenue recovered), not features consumed. The customer should always feel that the subscription pays for itself many times over. Every pricing page, email, and dashboard should reinforce the ROI equation.

### Tier Structure

**Solo — $49/month**
- Target: Individual freelancer, consultant, creator
- Includes: 1 AI agent, 100 calls/month, basic follow-up sequences, appointment booking, call transcripts
- Overage: $0.50/call
- Positioning: "Your personal revenue assistant"

**Business — $297/month**
- Target: Single-location service business (HVAC, dental, legal, med spa)
- Includes: 3 AI agents, 500 calls/month, full follow-up engine, no-show recovery, reactivation campaigns, industry templates, analytics dashboard, SMS + email
- Overage: $0.30/call
- Positioning: "The complete revenue execution system"

**Scale — $997/month**
- Target: Multi-location, high-volume, sales teams
- Includes: 10 AI agents, 3,000 calls/month, everything in Business + advanced analytics, team management, custom workflows, priority support, API access
- Overage: $0.20/call
- Positioning: "Enterprise-grade execution at scale"

**Enterprise — Custom ($2,400-$25,000+/month)**
- Target: Franchise operations, agencies, large multi-location
- Includes: Unlimited agents, custom call volume, white-label, dedicated account manager, SLA, SSO, custom integrations, on-premises voice option
- Positioning: "Built for your organization"

### Premium Add-Ons (Upsell Opportunities)

### Add-On 1: Custom Voice Training ($500-2000/month)

**What it is**: Train AI to sound exactly like customer's brand voice (or specific person)

**How it works**:
- Customer provides 5-10 min of audio (their rep, founder, etc.)
- RECALL TOUCH fine-tunes LLM on that voice
- AI speaks in that person's voice/tone/cadence

**Who buys it**: 
- Large enterprises wanting brand consistency
- Agencies wanting to white-label
- High-prestige brands (luxury, financial)

**Pricing**: $500-2000/month depending on customization depth

**Margin**: High (mostly engineering effort upfront, recurring revenue)

### Add-On 2: Real-Time Voice Customization ($200-500/month)

**What it is**: Advanced voice options (different accents, tones, emotional qualities)

**How it works**:
- Select from 20+ pre-trained voices (not just 5)
- Choose tone: Professional, friendly, urgent, empathetic, etc.
- Set delivery speed/cadence

**Who buys it**: Teams wanting to match voice to use case (churn prevention = empathetic, sales = confident)

**Pricing**: $200-500/month depending on options

**Margin**: Medium (server costs for multiple voice models)

### Add-On 3: Priority Implementation & Training ($1000-5000, one-time)

**What it is**: Dedicated person helps set up, builds templates, trains team

**How it works**:
- 2-4 hour onboarding session with customer success manager
- Build 3-5 custom campaigns based on customer's use cases
- Train team on best practices
- 30-day post-implementation check-in

**Who buys it**: Teams that want hand-holding, don't want to figure it out alone

**Pricing**: $1000-5000 depending on complexity (typically $2000 for mid-market)

**Margin**: High (mostly human time, billed at $200-500/hour)

### Add-On 4: Advanced Analytics & Custom Reporting ($200-500/month)

**What it is**: Custom dashboards, predictive analytics, automated reporting

**How it works**:
- Build custom dashboard (conversion funnel, revenue pipeline, churn risk)
- Automated weekly/monthly reports emailed to leadership
- Predictive: "Based on current calling, you'll close X deals by month end"
- Integrate with BI tools (Tableau, Looker)

**Who buys it**: Operations-focused, data-driven teams

**Pricing**: $200-500/month

**Margin**: Medium (requires engineering to build integrations)

### Add-On 5: Dedicated Account Manager ($500-2000/month)

**What it is**: Human point of contact, strategic guidance, campaign optimization

**How it works**:
- Assigned account manager (knows customer's business, goals)
- Monthly 1-hour strategy call
- Proactive optimization: "Try this script variation, it might increase conversion"
- Priority support: 1-hour response time
- Quarterly business review with metrics

**Who buys it**: Teams wanting to maximize ROI, get best results, have complex needs

**Pricing**: $500-2000/month depending on customer size

**Margin**: Low-medium (human time intensive, but recurring)

**Note**: Business tier includes "customer success manager" (quarterly check-ins). This add-on is more frequent + strategic.

### Add-On 6: White-Label / Agency Program ($2000-10,000/month)

**What it is**: Rebrand RECALL TOUCH as your own platform, resell to clients

**How it works**:
- Customers see your branding (your logo, your domain, your colors)
- You set your own pricing
- RECALL TOUCH handles delivery, you handle sales + support
- Economics: You buy at $300/user/month (example), resell at $500+

**Who buys it**: Agencies, consulting firms, outsourced sales companies

**Pricing**: Tiered based on resale volume
- <10 end-customers: $2000/month
- 10-50 end-customers: $5000/month
- 50+ end-customers: $10,000/month or revenue-share (20-30%)

**Margin**: High for RECALL TOUCH (white-label setup cost upfront, recurring fee thereafter)

### Add-On 7: API Access & Custom Integrations ($200-1000/month)

**What it is**: Webhooks, API keys, ability to build custom workflows

**How it works**:
- Get API documentation
- Build custom integrations (call RECALL TOUCH from your system, send results anywhere)
- Support for webhook failures, retry logic
- Included in Business tier, add-on for Professional

**Who buys it**: Teams with custom tech stacks, engineering-heavy orgs

**Pricing**: $200-1000/month depending on complexity

**Margin**: Medium (mostly support cost)

---

## Feature Gating (What's Included at Each Level)

**Feature: Basic Calling**
- Starter: ✓ (limited templates)
- Professional: ✓ (all templates, custom scripts)
- Business: ✓ (everything)
- Enterprise: ✓ (everything + custom)

**Feature: CRM Integration**
- Starter: Salesforce, HubSpot, or Pipedrive (pick one)
- Professional: All CRMs + webhooks
- Business: All CRMs + webhooks + API
- Enterprise: All CRMs + webhooks + API + custom

**Feature: Multi-Channel Sequences**
- Starter: ✗
- Professional: ✓ (email, SMS, WhatsApp)
- Business: ✓ (everything + scheduling)
- Enterprise: ✓ (everything + custom channels)

**Feature: Team Collaboration**
- Starter: ✗ (single user)
- Professional: ✓ (10 users, basic roles)
- Business: ✓ (unlimited users, advanced roles)
- Enterprise: ✓ (unlimited users, granular permissions)

**Feature: Analytics**
- Starter: Basic dashboard (calls, success rate)
- Professional: Advanced dashboard + A/B testing
- Business: Everything + predictive analytics + custom reports
- Enterprise: Everything + BI integration

**Feature: Support**
- Starter: Email support (48-hour response)
- Professional: Email + priority (4-hour response) + QSM check-ins
- Business: Email + priority (1-hour) + dedicated account manager
- Enterprise: Email + phone + dedicated engineer, <1-hour response

---

## Performance-Based Pricing (Alternative Model)

**What it is**: Pay based on actual results (meetings booked, deals closed), not usage

**Model**: 
- Base fee: $100-500/month (covers infrastructure)
- Success fee: $50-200 per meeting booked, or 10-20% of deal value closed

**Pros:**
- Customer only pays if it works (removes risk)
- Aligns incentives (RECALL TOUCH is motivated to make sales)
- High perceived value (customer feels like they're getting deal)

**Cons:**
- Complex to implement (need to verify meetings booked, deals closed)
- Fraud risk (customer books fake meetings, RECALL TOUCH pays)
- Unpredictable revenue for RECALL TOUCH
- Requires CRM integration to track

**Recommendation**: Offer as optional tier for high-volume enterprise customers (after they've proven ROI with traditional pricing). Example: "Instead of paying per call, pay per qualified meeting booked."

---

## Best Initial Pricing (Market Entry Strategy)

**Recommendation for Launch:**

**Tier 1: Starter - $99/month**
- Cheap enough to feel like "free trial" upgrade
- Accessible to solopreneurs and small teams
- Builds volume of users

**Tier 2: Professional - $299/month**
- Sweet spot for growing companies
- 3x price from Starter, but 10x more calls
- Where most revenue comes from

**Tier 3: Business - $999/month**
