## PART 5 — BILLING / PRICING LOGIC

### Plan Definitions

**Solo Plan - $29/month**
- 100 calls/month included
- 1 user
- 500 contacts
- 3 active sequences
- Basic support (email)
- Features: manual contacts, basic SMS templates, call recording, basic reporting
- Overage: $0.25/call over 100

**Starter Plan - $79/month**
- 500 calls/month included
- Up to 3 users
- 2,000 contacts
- 10 active sequences
- Unlimited SMS (Twilio rates apply)
- 1 GB storage
- Workflow automation (basic triggers only)
- Email support + community Slack
- Features: CRM import, advanced templates, basic AI responses
- Overage: $0.20/call, $0.01/SMS, $0.05/AI response

**Growth Plan - $199/month**
- 2,000 calls/month included
- Up to 10 users
- 10,000 contacts
- 50 active sequences
- Advanced workflow engine (multi-trigger, conditional logic)
- Custom voice profiles (basic training: up to 3 voice datasets)
- Voice quality evaluation included (up to 5 evaluations/month)
- 10 GB storage
- Stripe + Zapier integrations included
- Phone support
- Advanced reporting (funnel, cohort, revenue attribution)
- Overage: $0.15/call, $0.01/SMS, $0.05/AI response, $0.50/voice training minute (beyond included)

**Scale Plan - $499/month**
- 5,000 calls/month included
- Up to 25 users
- 50,000 contacts
- Unlimited active sequences
- Advanced workflow engine + custom triggers (webhook, API)
- Unlimited custom voice profiles
- Voice quality evaluation (unlimited)
- Voice datasets (up to 10 per voice, unlimited storage)
- Pronunciation rules (up to 500 custom rules)
- 100 GB storage
- Full CRM integration suite (Salesforce, HubSpot, Pipedrive, custom)
- Slack + Teams + Zapier + custom webhooks
- Dedicated account manager
- Phone + Slack priority support
- Advanced analytics (predictive churn, LTV cohort, attribution modeling)
- A/B testing for sequences
- White-label branding option (+$500/month)
- Overage: $0.10/call, $0.01/SMS, $0.05/AI response, $0.25/voice training minute

**Enterprise Plan - Custom**
- Custom call volume
- Unlimited users
- Unlimited contacts
- Unlimited sequences + workflows
- Dedicated infrastructure option (self-hosted or isolated cloud)
- Custom voice profile SLA (training turnaround within 48h)
- Voice inference latency SLA (< 100ms p95)
- White-label + co-branded support
- Custom integrations development (estimate 100h @ $200/h)
- Security: SOC 2 Type II compliance, HIPAA (if healthcare), data residency options
- Quarterly business reviews + strategy sessions
- On-premises deployment option (add 30-40% to contract value)

### Included Usage Per Plan

| Feature | Solo | Starter | Growth | Scale | Enterprise |
|---------|------|---------|--------|-------|-----------|
| Calls/month | 100 | 500 | 2,000 | 5,000 | Custom |
| Voice training minutes/month | 0 | 0 | 50 | 200 | Custom |
| Voice quality evaluations/month | 0 | 0 | 5 | Unlimited | Unlimited |
| Custom voice profiles | 0 | 0 | 3 | Unlimited | Unlimited |
| Pronunciation rules | 0 | 0 | 0 | 500 | Unlimited |
| Users | 1 | 3 | 10 | 25 | Unlimited |
| Contacts | 500 | 2,000 | 10,000 | 50,000 | Unlimited |
| Storage | 1 GB | 1 GB | 10 GB | 100 GB | Unlimited |
| SMS | 50 included | 100 included | 500 included | Unlimited | Unlimited |
| API calls/day | 1,000 | 5,000 | 50,000 | 500,000 | Custom |

### Overage Rates

- **Calls**: $0.25 (Solo), $0.20 (Starter), $0.15 (Growth), $0.10 (Scale)
- **SMS**: $0.01/SMS all plans (Twilio pass-through; billed real-time)
- **Voice training**: $0.50/min (Starter/Growth), $0.25/min (Scale); included volume first
- **Voice inference**: included in call metering; no separate charge
- **Storage**: $0.05/GB/month over included limit
- **Seats**: $29/seat/month (Solo → Starter), $99/seat/month (Growth → Scale)
- **API calls**: billed on daily peak; if 1,050 calls in day, charged $0.10 for 50 overage (capped example rate)
- **Custom integrations**: $200/hour billed monthly on cost basis

### Setup & Onboarding Charges

- **Setup fee**: $0 (Solo), $0 (Starter), $500 (Growth onward, waived first 3 months)
- **Custom voice training setup**: $250 per voice (if using self-hosted Fish Speech; ElevenLabs tier 2 voices = $100 credit + monthly subscription model)
- **CRM integration setup**: Included if pre-configured (Salesforce, HubSpot, Pipedrive); custom integrations = $500–$2,000 (estimate)
- **Data migration**: $250 (up to 10k contacts), $500 (up to 50k contacts), $1,000+ (custom datasets)

### Add-Ons

- **White-label branding**: $500/month (custom domain, logo, email templates, branded mobile app) — Growth+
- **Dedicated account manager**: $300/month — Starter+
- **Advanced voice profiles (beyond included)**:
  - ElevenLabs Professional Voices: $99/month/voice (access to 100+ voices, priority support)
  - Custom trained voice (Fish Speech): $250 setup + $50/month storage/inference
- **Priority phone support**: $100/month — Starter+
- **Slack integration + notifications**: Included Growth+; $50/month Starter
- **HIPAA compliance**: $2,000 setup + $500/month ongoing (Growth+)
- **SOC 2 Type II audit report**: Included Scale+; $5,000 one-time Growth
- **Custom API rate limit tier**: $100/month per 100k calls/day increase
- **API logging & webhooks**: Included Growth+; $50/month Starter
- **On-premises deployment**: +40% of annual contract value (Setup $10k–$50k depending on complexity)

### Seat & Location Logic

- **User seats**: count of active users; billed monthly in arrears
- **Location add-on**: if org has multiple locations (locations table), charge per location (locations > 1):
  - Growth: $50/location/month
  - Scale: $100/location/month
  - Enterprise: included
- **Team seats**: don't charge extra per team; just per user across all teams
- **Department cost allocation**: if org enables cost center tracking, split call/SMS/training costs by cost_center_code; show breakdown in admin billing dashboard

### Agency & White-Label Logic

- **White-label option**: Growth+ plans can enable custom domain, logo, email templates, phone support branding
- **Agency reseller program**: partner organizations can purchase bulk seats at 40% discount; resell to end customers at markup; billing flows through partner org
- **Multi-customer management**: partner can create sub-organizations under their master org; each sub-org has isolated data + separate billing
- **Revenue share**: partner receives 20% of revenue from sub-org seats; tracked in partner admin dashboard

### Margin Guardrails

- **Cost-to-serve tracking**: backend tracks actual cost of calls (Twilio $0.05–$0.15/min), SMS ($0.01/message), voice ($Fish Speech $0.001/char, ElevenLabs variable), inference/training; flag if margin falls below 50%
- **Pricing floor**: never discount below 40% margin; if customer tries to negotiate below floor, escalate to finance
- **Volume-based margin**: customers with >100k calls/month automatically moved to Scale or Enterprise; adjust pricing if margin below 45%
- **Profitability monitoring**: daily dashboard for CFO/ops showing margin % by plan, by customer, by feature; flag red zones (<40% margin)
- **Sunset unprofitable features**: if custom voice training/inference costs exceed revenue from feature, deprecate or re-price

### Voice Premium Tier

- **ElevenLabs Premium Voices** (Starter+): $99/month per org, access to 100+ premium voices (celebrity, specialized accents, emotional range)
- **Custom Trained Voices** (Growth+): $250 one-time setup per voice + $50/month per voice (storage + inference optimization)
- **Voice Cloning** (Scale+): Enterprise feature; $1,000 per cloned voice (requires audio samples from customer); inference cost includes in call pricing
- **Pronunciation Rule Premium** (Growth+): up to 50 rules free; $1/rule/month for additional (limit 500 per org)

### Custom Voice Pricing

- **Training cost model**:
  - Per minute of training data: $0.50/min (Growth), $0.25/min (Scale)
  - Minimum training set: 10 minutes audio; $5 (Growth), $2.50 (Scale)
  - Rush training (24h turnaround): +100% premium
  
- **Inference cost model**:
  - Included in call pricing (no separate charge)
  - If organization uses voice for non-call channels (SMS TTS read-aloud, email summaries), charge $0.001/character
  
- **Quality tier pricing**:
  - Standard (MOS 3.5–4.0): $0.25/min training + base inference
  - Premium (MOS 4.0–4.5): +$0.10/min training + $0.001 character inference
  - Ultra (MOS 4.5+): +$0.25/min training + $0.002/character inference

---

## PART 6 — ANALYTICS / KPI REQUIREMENTS

### Response Speed (Omnichannel)
- **Definition**: Time from contact message (call, SMS, email) → first response (agent or AI)
- **Metric variants**:
  - Call response time: inbound call → outbound callback (minutes)
  - Missed-call response time: call missed → SMS/callback sent (minutes)
  - SMS response time: SMS received → SMS reply (minutes)
  - Email response time: email received → reply sent (hours)
- **Targets**:
  - Calls: 95th percentile < 30min (real estate benchmark: 5min for hot leads)
  - SMS: 95th percentile < 2min
  - Email: 95th percentile < 4 hours
- **Dashboard display**: response time distribution histogram, p50/p95/p99, trend over time (7d, 30d)
- **Alerts**: if p95 > target for >4 hours, notify assigned rep

### Booked Appointments
- **Definition**: Total confirmed appointments (booking.status = confirmed) in period
- **Variants**:
  - Booked via system (contact scheduled via SMS link or IVR)
  - Booked via agent (agent created booking after call)
  - Booked via callback (contact left voicemail, system scheduled callback, callback resulted in booking)
- **Metrics**: count, trend (daily/weekly), % of total opportunities, booking value (sum of opportunity.value for booked)
- **Attribution**: link to conversation_id, workflow_id, sequence_id (which workflow/sequence led to booking)
- **Dashboard**: KPI box, trend chart (7d/30d), breakdown by source, by rep, by workflow

### Missed-Call Recovery Rate
- **Definition**: % of missed calls that were successfully recovered (callback attempted and contact responded)
- **Formula**: (successful recoveries / total missed calls) × 100
- **Tracking**:
  - Missed call triggered → missed-call workflow executed → SMS/callback sent → if contact called back or responded = recovery success
  - Recovery considered success if: (a) contact answered callback, (b) contact responded to SMS
- **Targets**: 25–40% for B2C, 40–60% for B2B (higher persistence)
- **Dashboard**: KPI, trend line, breakdown by recovery method (SMS vs callback), by team

### No-Show Recovery Rate
- **Definition**: % of booked appointments marked as no_show where recovery action succeeded
- **Formula**: (successful recoveries / total no-shows) × 100
- **Tracking**:
  - Booking marked no_show → no-show workflow executed (immediate SMS + task + callback) → if contact rescheduled or reschedule attempted = recovery success
  - Success: contact reschedules or commits to new time
  - Partial success: contact responds but doesn't reschedule
  - Failure: no response
- **Targets**: 20–30% (industry benchmark: 15%)
- **Dashboard**: KPI, recovery attempt timeline (immediate, +1h, +6h, +24h), success rate by recovery method

### Reactivation Wins
- **Definition**: Opportunities reopened from closed/lost stage OR contacts re-engaged after 60+ days of inactivity
- **Tracking**:
  - Opportunity stage changed from (lost → active stage) OR contact reactivated after inactivity_flag = true
  - Win value: if reactivation resulted in booking/closed deal, log revenue
  - Reason: captured in event.metadata.reason (e.g., "follow-up sequence", "missed-call recovery")
- **Metrics**: count (reactivations), value (sum), conversion rate (reactivations → booking/closed)
- **Dashboard**: KPI (count + value), breakdown by reason, by contact segment, trend (quarterly)

### Revenue Influenced & Revenue Recovered
- **Revenue Influenced**: Total value of opportunities that progressed stage or closed within 7 days of contact (calls, SMS, workflows)
  - Tracked via event.metadata.revenue_amount when opportunity stage changes
  - Attribution: link to workflow_id, sequence_id, conversation_id
  - Exclude: opportunities that were already in advanced stage (proposal/negotiation)
  - Calculation: sum of opportunity.value where stage_before < stage_after, within 7d of contact event
  
- **Revenue Recovered**: Value of opportunities reopened from lost stage OR no-show appointments successfully rescheduled/recovered
  - Tracked via event.type = recovery with recovery_win_value in metadata
  - Calculation: sum of recovery_win_value where recovery_status = success
  
- **Metrics**: 30-day sum, month-over-month trend, per rep, per workflow/sequence
- **Dashboard**: stacked bar chart (revenue influenced vs recovered over time), breakdown by source, attribution to workflows
- **Targets**: Aim for 30–50% of monthly revenue to be influenced by system (varies by industry)

### Pipeline Progression
- **Definition**: Movement of opportunities through sales stages; measure velocity and drop-off
- **Metrics**:
  - Funnel: count of opportunities by stage; drop-off % (stage_A → stage_B)
  - Velocity: average time from initial contact → qualified → proposal → closed (by stage)
  - Conversion rate: (opportunities closed won) / (total opportunities) × 100
  - Stalled deals: opportunities in stage > 30 days without activity
  
- **Dashboard**: 
  - Funnel chart: visual funnel showing count and % at each stage
  - Time-in-stage: box plot showing distribution (p25/p50/p75) days per stage
  - Stage conversion heatmap: opportunity source vs stage; identify bottleneck sources
  - Stalled deals list: flagged for followup

### Usage Metrics (By Plan)
- **Calls**: total calls made (all channels), breakdown by channel (voice, SMS, email), daily average
- **Contacts**: count of active contacts (last interaction < 90d), count by source, growth rate
- **Workflows**: count of active workflows, count of executions (daily/weekly), avg execution time
- **Sequences**: count of active sequences, count of enrollments, avg steps, avg time-to-completion
- **API calls**: daily count, breakdown by endpoint, error rate (4xx/5xx)
- **Storage**: total GB used (calls + transcripts + custom voice datasets + user uploads)
- **Users**: active user count (last login < 7d), user growth
- **Seats**: current seat count, forecast (if adding users regularly)
- **Dashboard**: usage meter (% of plan limit), trend (30d), overage risk alert (if >80% of limit)

### Cost-to-Serve
- **Definition**: Total cost of infrastructure + third-party services to deliver outcomes (calls, SMS, responses)
- **Components**:
  - Twilio calls: $0.05–$0.15/min (depends on VCN, geography, peak times)
  - Twilio SMS: $0.01/SMS
  - Fish Speech TTS (self-hosted): $0.0005/character (amortized server cost)
  - ElevenLabs TTS: $0.03/1k characters
  - Faster-Whisper STT: $0.001/min (amortized GPU cost)
  - Supabase hosting: $50–$500/month (scales with usage)
  - AWS S3 storage: $0.023/GB/month (for recordings + datasets)
  - Stripe processing: 2.9% + $0.30 per transaction
  
- **Tracking**: billing_events table records all cost-generating events; sum by period
- **Metrics**: 
  - Cost per call: total_cost / call_count
  - Cost per booking: total_cost / bookings_created
  - Cost per revenue_dollar: total_cost / revenue_influenced (ROI inverse)
  
- **Alerts**: if cost_per_call rises 10% month-over-month or cost_per_booking exceeds target, flag for ops review
- **Dashboard** (admin only): cost breakdown by feature, monthly spend, margin % (plan revenue - cogs), forecast

### Churn-Risk Signals
- **Behavioral signals**:
  - Declining call volume (>50% drop week-over-week)
  - No logins by admin for >14 days
  - Declining bookings (>50% drop week-over-week)
  - Missed payments (stripe_subscription_status = past_due for >7 days)
  - Support ticket spike (3+ tickets in 7 days indicating frustration)
  
- **Predictive model** (if ML implemented):
  - Input features: plan tenure, monthly calls, monthly revenue influenced, user engagement score, cost-to-serve ratio, support ticket count
  - Output: churn probability (0–100%); flag accounts >50% as high-risk
  
- **Actions**:
  - Flag high-risk accounts in admin dashboard (red zone)
  - Trigger outreach workflow (send account manager email, offer onboarding call, special offer if willing to share feedback)
  - Alert ops if Scale/Enterprise account at risk
  
- **Dashboard**: churn risk heatmap (customer × risk score), cohort churn rate (by acquisition month), reasons for churn (post-cancel survey)

### Voice-Specific KPIs

**Voice Latency**
- **Definition**: End-to-end time from request to synthesized audio ready to play
- **Formula**: time(audio returned) - time(synthesis request initiated)
- **Measurement**: tracked in voice_usage_records.latency_ms; aggregated daily
- **Targets**:
  - Fish Speech (self-hosted): p95 < 100ms
  - ElevenLabs: p95 < 300ms
- **Dashboard**: p50/p95/p99 latency, trend (7d/30d), breakdown by voice profile, by inference provider
- **Alerts**: if p95 latency > target for >10 min, trigger fallback provider

**Voice Quality Score**
- **Definition**: Mean Opinion Score (MOS) derived from quality_evaluation_records
- **Calculation**: avg of clarity_score + naturalness_score + intelligibility_score (each 1-10 scale) / 3; scaled to 0-100
- **Measurement**: evaluations performed on trained voices; custom trained voices evaluated pre-activation
- **Targets**:
  - Minimum to activate: MOS 3.5 (acceptable quality)
  - High quality: MOS 4.0+ (good)
  - Premium: MOS 4.5+ (excellent)
- **Dashboard**: MOS trend per voice profile, comparison (custom voice vs ElevenLabs baseline)
- **Alerts**: if voice quality degrades (MOS drops >0.5 in 30d), flag for retraining

**Voice Interruption Rate**
- **Definition**: % of voice calls where user interrupted while voice was playing
- **Tracking**: conversation_metadata tracks user_interrupted_at_timestamp; compute rate = interruptions / total_voice_calls
- **Causes****: aggressive TTS, user didn't understand initial prompt, timeout to user input was too long
- **Targets**: <15% (higher interruption = user confusion)
- **Dashboard**: interruption rate trend, breakdown by voice profile, by contact segment
- **Actions**: if >15%, trigger voice retraining or prompt optimization

**Conversion by Voice Profile**
- **Definition**: Conversion rate (booking / total calls) for each voice profile
- **Tracking**: conversation.voice_profile_id linked to outcome; compute conversion_rate = bookings / total_calls
- **Comparison**: compare custom voice vs. default vs. ElevenLabs voices; identify if certain voices perform better
- **Dashboard**: bar chart by voice profile, sorted by conversion rate; include sample size (call count)
- **Insights**: if custom voice underperforms by >5%, flag for quality review or A/B test replacement

---

## PART 7 — INFRASTRUCTURE / COST-CONTROL REQUIREMENTS

### Usage Metering

- **Metering agent**: background service that ingests events from Kafka stream or Bull queue
- **Event types metered**:
  - call_completed: extract duration_seconds, contact_id, conversation_id; emit billing_event
  - sms_sent: extract sms_count, contact_id; emit billing_event
  - ai_response: extract token_count (from LLM response); emit billing_event
  - voice_inference: record start_time, end_time (call duration); emit voice_usage_record with inference_seconds
  - voice_training: on training_job completion, record total_minutes; emit billing_event
  - storage: daily batch job counts S3 objects by organization; emit usage_record
  - api_calls: request middleware increments counter; daily batch emit
  
- **Real-time aggregation**: Redis cache stores current month's usage (calls, SMS, tokens, voice minutes) per organization; refreshed every 5 min
- **Batch write**: every 1 hour, flush Redis cache to billing_events + usage_records tables (idempotent writes)
- **Stripe sync**: every 6 hours, query billing_events since last sync; post to Stripe Billing Meters API to report usage
- **Accuracy**: implement idempotency keys (conversation_id, call_sid) to prevent double-counting if retries occur

### Per-Feature Cost Attribution

- **Call metering**: per_call_cost = base_rate (plan-dependent) + vcn_premium (if VCN) + duration_overage
- **SMS metering**: per_sms_cost = $0.01 fixed (Twilio pass-through)
- **AI response metering**: per_response_cost = (token_count / 1000) × $0.01 (estimate for GPT-4 or Claude)
- **Voice training metering**: per_minute_cost = training_rate (plan-dependent: $0.50–$0.25/min)
- **Voice inference metering**: included in call cost (no separate charge); if used outside calls, $0.001/char
- **Storage metering**: per_gb_cost = $0.05/GB/month over included limit
- **Location add-on**: per_location_cost = $50–$100/month (plan-dependent)
- **Seat metering**: per_seat_cost = $29–$99/month (plan-dependent)
- **Custom integrations**: lump-sum cost (billed at project completion)

- **Attribution logic**: for each billing_event or usage_record, compute cost; store in billing_event.total_cost; sum monthly for invoice
- **Dashboard** (admin): breakdown chart showing cost by feature; identify high-cost features (e.g., heavy voice training)

### Batching & Caching

- **Call batching**: don't initiate Twilio call immediately on user request; batch and queue calls every 10 seconds (max 50 calls per batch) if volume >10/sec
  - Benefit: reduced Twilio API calls + connection overhead; max latency increase <10s
  - Exception: high-priority calls (hot leads flagged in UI) bypass batching; immediate initiation
  
- **SMS batching**: queue SMS messages; batch every 5 sec or max 100 messages; post to Twilio in single API call
  - Benefit: 90% reduction in API calls; max latency <5s
  
- **Transcription batching**: defer transcription until call_ended; batch all pending transcriptions every 2 min; ship to Faster-Whisper worker pool
  - Benefit: better GPU utilization; transcription latency 2–5min (acceptable for async review)
  
- **Caching strategy**:
  - **Contact 360 cache**: Redis TTL 1 hour; invalidate on contact update
  - **Voice profile cache**: Redis TTL 24 hours; store voice_id → provider_id + config
  - **Template cache**: Redis TTL 24 hours; store template_id → content + variables
  - **Org config cache**: Redis TTL 24 hours; store org settings, industry pack, RLS rules
  - **CRM sync cache**: Redis TTL 30 min; store last-sync timestamp, pending updates
  
- **Cache invalidation**: on entity update (contact, template, workflow), emit event; cache layer subscribes and invalidates (publish-subscribe pattern)

### Async Job Processing

- **Job queue system**: Bull (Node.js) + Redis backend
- **Job types**:
  - Voicemail transcription (priority: high, timeout: 5min, max retries: 3)
  - Sequence step execution (priority: medium, timeout: 1min, max retries: 2)
  - No-show recovery workflow (priority: high, timeout: 10min, max retries: 1)
  - Reminder dispatch (priority: low, timeout: 30s, max retries: 1)
  - Data export (priority: low, timeout: 60min, max retries: 0)
  - Analytics aggregation (priority: low, timeout: 30min, max retries: 0)
  - Voice training (priority: medium, timeout: 120min, max retries: 1)
  - Daily billing aggregation (priority: critical, timeout: 60min, max retries: 3)
  
- **Worker pool**: 4–8 workers per job type; auto-scale based on queue depth
- **Dead-letter queue**: jobs failing max retries → dead letter queue; alert admin daily; manual retry available
- **Job idempotency**: store job result keyed by [conversation_id + action_type]; skip if exists + created_at < 1min ago

### Vendor Failover

- **Phone service failover**: 
  - Primary: Twilio (99.99% uptime SLA)
  - Secondary: Bandwidth.com (alternative provider configured)
  - Logic: on Twilio API error (5xx or timeout), retry up to 3x with exponential backoff; if all fail, queue to Bandwidth fallback
  - Testing: monthly failover drill (simulate Twilio outage; verify calls route to Bandwidth)

- **SMS service failover**:
  - Primary: Twilio SMS
  - Secondary: AWS SNS
  - Logic: same as phone failover

- **Voice TTS failover**:
  - Primary: Fish Speech (self-hosted)
  - Secondary: ElevenLabs
  - Logic: on Fish Speech error or latency >1s, fallback to ElevenLabs for that request; log failover event
  
- **STT failover**:
  - Primary: Faster-Whisper (self-hosted)
  - Secondary: Twilio transcription
  - Logic: on Faster-Whisper error or queue depth >100, fallback to Twilio; capture transcription, compare quality

- **Database failover**: Supabase managed replication; if primary region down, auto-failover to replica (RTO <1min)

### Channel Fallback

- **Call channel fallback**:
  - Primary: live phone call (Twilio)
  - Secondary: voicemail (if no answer after 3 rings)
  - Tertiary: SMS (if voicemail full or call undeliverable)
  
- **Messaging channel fallback**:
  - Primary: SMS (if contact has phone)
  - Secondary: email (if contact has email, no phone)
  - Tertiary: in-app notification (if contact app user)

- **Voice fallback** (if custom voice unavailable):
  - Primary: assigned voice profile
  - Secondary: org default voice profile
  - Tertiary: system default voice (ElevenLabs English US female)

- **Configuration**: workflow engine respects channel fallback order; no manual override needed

### Cost Alerts

- **Real-time alerts**:
  - If daily spend > avg daily spend × 1.5, send admin email (daily at 6pm)
  - If monthly forecast (current spend × days_remaining / days_elapsed) > plan budget × 0.8, send email + in-app banner
  - If monthly forecast > plan budget × 1.2, send urgent email to billing contact + account manager
  
- **Spending guardrails** (hard limits, configurable):
  - If monthly spend > plan budget × 1.5, pause new workflow executions; alert admin for approval
  - If monthly spend > plan budget × 2.0, pause all non-critical actions; hard stop calls + SMS (except critical recovery actions)
  
- **Dashboard**: cost trend chart (daily/weekly), budget vs actual, forecast line; color-coded zones (green <80%, yellow 80–120%, red >120%)

### Margin Protection

- **Minimum margin enforcement**: for each billing_event, calculate cost (vendor cost) + gross_margin_buffer; if revenue for plan cannot sustain (plan_price * org_usage / quota * months_elapsed < cost * 1.5), flag account as unprofitable
- **Unprofitable account handling**:
  - Alert ops + finance (flag color: red)
  - If customer acquired <3 months ago: offer free onboarding call to optimize usage + reduce cost
  - If customer > 6 months: re-price plan (offer higher tier) or negotiate custom contract with volume discount
  - If margin remains <40% after 60 days: escalate to CFO for contract review or wind-down
  
- **Margin dashboard** (Finance view): 
  - Customer table: plan, MRR, cogs, margin %, gross margin $, churn risk
  - Filter: margin <40% (red), 40–50% (yellow), >50% (green)
  - Trend: margin % over 12 months; plot against company targets
  - Scenarios: if cost of Twilio/ElevenLabs increases 10%, show impact on margin

### GPU Scheduling

- **Self-hosted Fish Speech infrastructure**:
  - 2× NVIDIA A100 GPUs (shared between TTS inference + STT inference + voice training)
  - Inference priority: TTS > STT > training (strict ordering; training jobs queued, not preempted)
  - Time-of-day scheduling: during peak hours (9am–6pm), allocate 1 GPU to TTS + 1 to STT; during off-peak (6pm–9am), allocate all GPU capacity to training jobs
  
- **GPU utilization monitoring**:
  - Prometheus metrics: GPU memory %, GPU utilization %, queue depth per service
  - Auto-scale alert: if GPU utilization >90% for >5min, alert ops to consider additional GPUs
  - Cost tracking: A100 cost ~$1.30/hour; track hourly usage; allocate to organizations (cost attribution via voice_inference minutes)

### Inference Tiering

- **Tier 1 (Real-time inference, latency <100ms)**:
  - Served from cache if available (hash text + voice_profile_id)
  - If cache miss, use Fish Speech (self-hosted GPU) or ElevenLabs premium endpoint
  - Cost: $0.001/char (amortized); billed via voice_inference metering
  - Use case: live calls, interactive responses
  
- **Tier 2 (Async inference, latency <10s)**:
  - Queued to Fish Speech or ElevenLabs standard endpoint
  - Cost: $0.0005/char (50% discount for batch processing)
  - Use case: SMS template generation, email body synthesis (read-aloud feature)
  
- **Tier 3 (Batch inference, latency <1 hour)**:
  - Accumulated and processed in off-peak hours (midnight–6am) on spare GPU capacity
  - Cost: $0.0001/char (90% discount)
  - Use case: sequence template pre-rendering, training dataset generation
  
- **Routing logic**: workflow action specifies tier requirement; system routes accordingly. Default = Tier 1 for calls, Tier 2 for SMS/email

### Voice Caching

- **Cache key**: MD5(text_content + voice_profile_id + speed + pitch)
- **Cache storage**: S3 voice_cache/ bucket; lifecycle policy (30-day TTL for unused)
- **Cache hit logic**: 
  - Inbound request for TTS; compute cache key
  - Check S3; if exists and <30 days old, return cached audio URL (redirect to signed S3 URL)
  - If miss or expired, synthesize, upload to S3, update expiry, return
- **Cache hit rate target**: 40–60% (many sequences use same templates; high hit rate reduces synthesis cost)
- **Cost savings**: if cache hit avoids ElevenLabs call ($0.03/1k chars) and uses cached S3 URL ($0.0023/GB for retrieval), savings ~90% per hit

### Training Queue Priorities

- **Queue tiers**:
  - Priority 1 (Urgent): customer onboarding, SLA-bound training (24h turnaround promised)
  - Priority 2 (High): customer-initiated training jobs (will be ready same week)
  - Priority 3 (Normal): scheduled training, non-blocking
  - Priority 4 (Low): internal tests, demo datasets
  
- **GPU allocation**:
  - If Priority 1 job queued, pause Priority 3/4 training; resume after Priority 1 completes
  - Estimate: Priority 1 job (10 min audio) trains in ~30 min on A100; can fit 2–3 Priority 1 jobs per day before impacting customer inference
  
- **SLA tracking**: training_job.expected_completion_at calculated (now + priority_factor * training_minutes); alert ops if lagging

---

## PART 8 — ROLLOUT ORDER

### Week 1–2: Foundation & Auth
- **User management**: user registration, email verification, password reset, OAuth (Google, Microsoft), sessions/JWT
- **Organization setup**: org creation (Stripe customer + subscription initialization), team + location setup, role + permission system (RBAC)
- **Database schema**: all tables from Part 2 created + indexed; RLS policies enabled
- **Supabase integration**: auth provider linked, storage bucket configured, real-time subscriptions enabled
- **Core API routes**: /api/auth/*, /api/orgs/*, /api/users/*, /api/teams/* (CRUD with RLS)
- **UI foundation**: Layout (navbar, sidebar, workspace selector), login/signup pages, org onboarding wizard (step 1–3)

### Week 3–4: Core Contact & Conversation
- **Contact management**: create, read, update, delete contacts; bulk import (CSV); tag system; custom fields (industry-specific)
- **Conversation ingestion**: Twilio webhook for inbound calls, SMS; store conversation records; conversation_status = pending/completed/missed
- **Call handling**: initiate outbound calls (Twilio), record call SID, link to conversation
- **SMS handling**: send + receive SMS (Twilio); store message thread
- **UI surfaces**: Contact list/card view, Contact detail timeline, Inbox (conversation list + detail), Call history
- **Basic reporting**: calls by day, conversations by status, contact count

### Month 2, Week 1–2: Workflows & Automation
- **Workflow engine**: trigger evaluation, condition matching, action dispatcher, retry mechanism
- **Workflow triggers**: conversation_outcome (booking, callback, interested, no_action), event-based (call_missed, appointment_no_show, conversion)
- **Workflow actions**: make_call, send_sms, send_email, create_task, update_opportunity, webhook
- **Workflow UI**: Visual workflow builder (React Flow), node palette, condition config, action config, publish + activate
- **Scheduling engine**: Cron evaluator, reminder dispatch (SMS/email), sequence step execution
- **Follow-up engine**: Missed-call recovery workflow, no-show recovery workflow, appointment confirmation reminders
- **UI surfaces**: Workflow list + builder, active workflow dashboard, workflow execution history

### Month 2, Week 3–4: Sequences & Templates
- **Sequence builder**: Timeline-based editor, step cards (action type, delay, template selector), branching (optional), A/B testing toggle
- **Template system**: Template CRUD, variable substitution ({{first_name}}, {{company}}, etc.), category system
- **Sequence enrollments**: Enroll contacts by tag or manual, track current step, schedule next step, completion tracking
- **Template gallery**: Industry-specific templates, system templates, org templates; preview + copy
- **Sequence performance**: Conversion rate by sequence, step-by-step analytics, A/B variant comparison
- **UI surfaces**: Sequence list + builder, enrollment list, template gallery, performance dashboard

### Month 2, Week 5+: Opportunities & Deals
- **Opportunity management**: Create, read, update, delete opportunities; link to contacts; stage progression (initial → qualified → proposal → won/lost)
- **Stage tracking**: log opportunity stage changes + timestamps; compute velocity (time in stage)
- **Opportunity linking**: link to conversations, workflows, sequences (attribution)
- **Funnel analytics**: visualize opportunities by stage, drop-off %, time-in-stage distribution
- **Revenue tracking**: log opportunity value, close date, closed won value (actual revenue); attribute to workflows/sequences
- **UI surfaces**: Opportunity Kanban board, opportunity detail, funnel analysis, revenue chart

### Month 3, Week 1–2: Analytics & Reporting
- **Core KPIs**: Response speed, booked appointments, conversion rate, revenue influenced, cost-to-serve
- **Real-time metrics**: Call count, SMS count, active conversations, pending tasks
- **Reporting UI**: Summary tab (KPI cards + charts), Funnel tab, Cohort tab, Revenue tab, Team Performance tab
- **Export**: download reports as CSV, Excel, PDF (via Bull job queue)
- **Custom reporting**: Report builder (drag/drop metrics + filters); schedule email delivery
- **Predictive analytics** (optional): Churn risk flagging, lead scoring model

### Month 3, Week 3–4: Voice Integration
- **Voice profile system**: Create voice profile (name, provider, language, gender, tone, speed, pitch); set as default
- **Voice preview**: Text input + play button; preview text with voice before deployment
- **ElevenLabs integration**: Fetch voice list, assign voice to conversation/workflow, synthesize + stream
- **Fallback voice**: If ElevenLabs fails, use system TTS (browser Web Audio)
- **Voice metering**: Track inference seconds per call; emit voice_usage_records; include in billing
- **UI surfaces**: Voice Library (profile list + create), Voice Preview, Voice assignment in workflows/contacts

### Month 3, Week 5+: Advanced Features (Concurrently or Sequential)
- **CRM integration**: Salesforce/HubSpot/Pipedrive OAuth + sync; two-way sync (create contact → pull to CRM, CRM update → pull to Recall Touch)
- **Slack integration**: Post conversation summaries, workflow alerts, booking notifications to Slack channel
- **Custom voice training**: Dataset upload, training job submission, quality evaluation, voice version activation
- **Pronunciation rules**: Define term → pronunciation mappings; apply to all voices
- **No-show recovery**: Auto-trigger recovery workflow on booking.status = no_show; immediate SMS + callback
- **Billing & Usage UI**: Plan display, usage meters, invoice list, cost alerts, upgrade/downgrade
- **Team admin**: Bulk user management, role assignment, activity audit, team-level reporting

### Month 4+: Polish & Scale
- **Performance optimization**: Database indexing, query optimization, caching layers, CDN for static assets
- **Mobile app** (optional): React Native app for iOS/Android; view inbox, make/receive calls, log outcomes
- **Advanced analytics**: Predictive churn model, LTV cohort analysis, attribution modeling
- **Integrations expansion**: Zapier, Make.com, custom webhooks; API documentation + SDK
- **White-label support**: Custom domain, logo, email branding; reseller program
- **Compliance**: SOC 2 audit, HIPAA (if healthcare), GDPR data export, retention policies
- **On-premises option**: Docker images for self-hosted deployment (if Enterprise customers request)

---

## PART 9 — DESIGN DIRECTION

### Philosophy
Premium, serious, mission-critical, operational. Built for professionals who need to rely on every feature daily. Modern but not trendy. Sharp, high-signal, low clutter. Non-generic; feels like a specialized tool, not a template.

### Color Palette
- **Primary**: Deep indigo (`#3B4BA0`) — trust, authority, tech-forward
- **Secondary**: Bright teal (`#00D4AA`) — energy, progress, action
- **Accent**: Warm amber (`#FFA800`) — urgency, highlights, CTAs
- **Neutral**: Charcoal (`#1A1A2E`), light gray (`#F5F5F8`), white (`#FFFFFF`)
- **Status colors**: 
  - Success/booking: Emerald green (`#10B981`)
  - Warning/missed-call: Amber (`#FFA800`)
  - Error/failed: Red (`#EF4444`)
  - Neutral/pending: Slate gray (`#64748B`)
- **Dark mode default**: Background `#0F172A`, surface `#1A2240`, text `#F1F5F9`

### Typography
- **Font stack**: Inter (headings + UI), Fira Code (monospace for transcripts + call SIDs)
- **Hierarchy**:
  - H1 (page titles): 32px, 700 weight, leading 1.2
  - H2 (section titles): 24px, 600 weight, leading 1.3
  - H3 (subsection titles): 18px, 600 weight
  - Body (default): 14px, 400 weight, leading 1.6
  - Small (labels, meta): 12px, 500 weight
  - Monospace (IDs, transcripts): 12px Fira Code, leading 1.4
- **Color**: Text on light = `#1A1A2E`; text on dark = `#F1F5F9`; muted = `#64748B`

### Spacing & Layout
- **Base unit**: 4px (4, 8, 12, 16, 24, 32, 40, 48, 64 px scale)
- **Container max-width**: 1400px; padding 16px mobile, 32px desktop
- **Grid**: 12-column, 16px gaps
- **Card elevation**: subtle shadows (0 2px 8px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.08) light; 0 4px 16px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.16) dark)
- **Rounded corners**: 6px (default), 8px (larger surfaces), 4px (small buttons + inputs)
- **Mobile margins**: 16px sides, 12px vertical gaps

### Component Style
- **Buttons**:
  - Primary (CTAs): indigo bg, white text, 8px h-padding, 32px h-height, rounded-6, no border, cursor pointer
  - Secondary (less prominent): transparent bg, indigo text, indigo 1px border, same sizing
  - Danger (delete, cancel): red text + border (secondary style)
  - Disabled: grayscale, cursor not-allowed, 50% opacity
  - Hover: 8% darker bg; subtle scale 1.02; 150ms transition
  - Active: scale 0.98, 50ms; visual feedback
  
- **Inputs**:
  - Border: 1px solid `#E2E8F0` (light), `#475569` (dark)
  - Padding: 8px 12px
  - Focus: blue outline 2px, offset 2px, no border color change (outline primary)
  - Font: 14px, body font stack, leading 1.4
  - Placeholder: `#9CA3AF`
  - Error state: red border, red bg 5% tint, error icon
  
- **Cards**:
  - Container: 6px rounded, 1px border `#E2E8F0` (light), bg white
  - Dark: bg `#1A2240`, border `#334155`
  - Padding: 16px–24px (spacing-6 to spacing-8)
  - Hover: shadow increase (if interactive)
  
- **Forms**:
  - Label above input (not placeholder)
  - Label: 12px, 500 weight, muted color, 4px margin below
  - Helper text: 12px, gray-500, below input
  - Error message: 12px, red, below input
  
- **Tables**:
  - Header row: bg `#F5F5F8` (light), `#1A2240` (dark), medium weight, left-aligned text
  - Data rows: alternating bg white / `#FAFBFC` (light), `#111827` / `#1A2240` (dark)
  - Row hover: highlight bg (2% darker)
  - Cell padding: 12px 8px (vertical × horizontal)
  - Dividers: 1px `#E2E8F0` (light), `#334155` (dark)
  
- **Modals**:
  - Backdrop: semi-transparent black (rgba 0,0,0,0.5), fade-in 150ms
  - Dialog: 400–600px width, centered, rounded-8, bg white/dark
  - Header: padding 20px, title font, close button (X) top-right
  - Body: padding 20px, scrollable if content >400px
  - Footer: padding 16px, buttons right-aligned, spacing-3 between buttons
  
- **Dropdowns**:
  - Trigger: button-like (border or transparent)
  - Menu: white/dark bg, rounded-6, shadow-lg, appear below trigger
  - Items: 36px height, padding 12px 16px, hover bg highlight, click triggers selection
  - Icons: 16px, left-aligned in item (optional)

### Animation Philosophy
- **Principle**: Micro-interactions, not eye candy. Purposeful, fast (150–300ms), easing function: cubic-bezier(0.4, 0, 0.2, 1) (subtle ease-in-out)
- **Hover states**: button scale 1.02 + shadow, 150ms
- **Open/close modals**: fade-in backdrop + scale-up dialog (from 0.95 → 1.0), 200ms
- **Page transitions**: subtle opacity fade (0 → 1), 100ms (not full slide animations)
- **Loading states**: rotating icon (spinner), calm gray, no flash
- **Success toast**: green bg, slide-in from bottom, auto-dismiss after 4s
- **Error alerts**: red bg + icon, persist until dismissed
- **Skeleton screens**: text-width placeholder blocks, gentle pulse animation (opacity 0.5 → 0.8 → 0.5), 1.5s cycle

### Dark Mode Default
- **Color mapping**:
  - Page bg: `#0F172A`
  - Surface bg (cards, modals): `#1A2240`
  - Dividers: `#334155`
  - Text: `#F1F5F9`
  - Muted text: `#CBD5E1`
  - Input bg: `#1A2240`
  - Input border: `#475569`
  - Input focus outline: bright teal `#00D4AA`
  - Button primary bg: indigo `#3B4BA0` (slightly lighter than light mode for contrast)
  - Button hover: `#4A5BB8`
  
- **Media**: Invert images by default (if predominantly light); provide light theme toggle in user preferences (stored in user.preferences)
- **Syntax highlighting** (transcripts, code): VS Code dark theme (One Dark Pro)

---

## PART 10 — FINAL ENGINEERING PRIORITIES

### Top 15 Most Important Items (In Exact Order)

1. **Authentication & Authorization System** (Week 1–2)
   - Supabase Auth (email + OAuth), JWT sessions, password reset
   - RBAC with granular permissions: contact.view, contact.create, workflow.execute, report.view, billing.manage
   - RLS policies on all tables; test that non-admins cannot query other org data
   - Rationale: Everything blocks on this; security-critical; all other features depend on identity

2. **Conversation Ingestion & Twilio Integration** (Week 1–2)
   - Webhook receiver for inbound calls (POST /webhook/twilio/call-inbound)
   - Parse Call SID, from_number, to_number, timestamp; create conversation record; route to contact lookup/create
   - Outbound call handler: accept workflow action, initiate Twilio call, track call_sid
   - Recording link storage + async transcription trigger
   - Rationale: Core revenue driver; every feature downstream depends on call data

3. **Core Data Model & RLS** (Week 1–2)
   - Supabase tables: users, organizations, teams, roles, contacts, conversations, workflows, sequences, opportunities, events
   - RLS policies: users can only read contacts assigned to them or their team; admins full access
   - Indexes on contact_id, organization_id, conversation_id, created_at for query performance
   - Rationale: Foundation for all subsequent features; multi-tenancy security

4. **Contact Management CRUD** (Week 1–2)
   - Create, read, update, delete contacts; soft delete (status = archived)
   - Bulk import (CSV parse + de-duplicate + validate phone); handle consent flags (voice_opt_in, sms_opt_in)
   - Contact detail view + timeline
   - Rationale: Users need to start building contact list immediately; required for MVP launch

5. **Workflow Engine & Trigger Evaluation** (Week 3–4)
   - Trigger evaluator: on conversation event (call_ended, sms_received), evaluate all active workflow conditions (conversation_status, intent_detected, tags, time window)
   - Action dispatcher: queue actions (call, SMS, task) with retry logic
   - Rate limiter: prevent spam (max X actions per contact per day)
   - Rationale: Automation is the product; without this, Recall Touch is just a call logger

6. **Billing Meter Integration with Stripe** (Week 2–3)
   - Metering agent ingests call_completed, sms_sent, voice_inference events
   - Emit events to Stripe Billing Meters API (real-time usage tracking)
   - Calculate overage charges based on plan limits
   - Display usage meters in billing dashboard
   - Rationale: Revenue-critical; if metering is wrong, company loses money; must be bulletproof + tested

7. **Voicemail Transcription Pipeline** (Week 3–4)
   - Async job: download Twilio voicemail recording, stream to Faster-Whisper (self-hosted STT)
   - Store transcript in conversation.transcript
   - Detect sentiment + intent from transcript (keywords: interested, objection, timeline, budget, authority)
   - Trigger voicemail-specific workflows (e.g., missed-call recovery)
   - Rationale: Voicemails are high-value for recovery; transcription + intent detection is a differentiator

8. **Basic Analytics Dashboard** (Week 3–4)
   - Real-time KPI boxes: calls today, booked appointments, conversion rate, response speed
   - Call trend chart (7d/30d)
   - Conversations by status (pie chart)
   - Rationale: Execs + sales managers need to see impact immediately; builds confidence in product

9. **Sequences & Templates System** (Month 2, Week 1–2)
   - Sequence CRUD: timeline-based editor, step delays, template assignment, publish/activate
   - Enrollment: automatically enroll contacts with matching tags; track current step + completion
   - Step execution: scheduled job checks due enrollments every 5 min; execute step action (SMS, call, email)
   - Template gallery: pre-built templates for common scenarios (initial outreach, follow-up, recovery)
   - Rationale: Sequences are the automation multiplier; save reps 5+ hours/week per sequence

10. **Follow-Up & Recovery Workflows** (Month 2, Week 1–2)
    - Missed-call recovery: on call_status = missed, trigger workflow, send SMS + schedule callback
    - No-show recovery: on booking_status = no_show, immediate callback attempt + SMS + task creation
    - Appointment confirmation: 24h + 2h reminder before booking
    - Rationale: Recovery is high-ROI; missed-call recovery ROI 3–5x cost; no-show recovery ROI 2–3x cost

11. **Custom Voice Integration (ElevenLabs)** (Month 3, Week 1)
    - Connect to ElevenLabs API; fetch voice list
    - Assign voice to organization (default) + contact (override) + workflow action
    - Synthesize voice for calls: on outbound call, send script to ElevenLabs, stream audio
    - Voice preview UI: text input + play button
    - Rationale: Voice is a major differentiator (vs. human agents reading scripts); high NPS booster

12. **Advanced Workflow Builder** (Month 2, Week 3–4)
    - Canvas-based editor (React Flow): trigger → conditions → actions → end
    - Condition nodes: conversation_outcome, contact_tags, date_range, custom_fields, CRM fields
    - Action nodes: make_call, send_sms, send_email, create_task, update_opportunity, webhook
    - Visual validation + error highlighting
    - Publish/version control + dry-run simulator
    - Rationale: Non-technical users (sales managers, ops) need to build workflows without coding; unlocks self-service

13. **Opportunity & Revenue Tracking** (Month 2, Week 4–5)
    - Opportunity CRUD: create from contact, link to conversations/workflows, stage progression
    - Revenue logging: log value, close date, attribution (which workflow/sequence moved deal)
    - Funnel analytics: visualize opportunities by stage, drop-off %, average time-in-stage
    - Revenue influenced metric: sum of opportunities moved to won within 7d of contact
    - Rationale: Sales leaders care about pipeline impact; revenue influenced is the key ROI metric

14. **Self-Hosted Voice Infrastructure** (Month 3, Week 2–3)
    - Deploy Fish Speech + Faster-Whisper on self-hosted GPU (EC2 instance with A100)
    - Inference endpoint for TTS: POST /synthesize with {text, voice_id, speed, pitch}
    - STT endpoint for transcription: POST /transcribe with audio stream
    - Cache synthesized audio in S3; serve from cache if hit (latency <50ms)
    - Latency monitoring: p95 <100ms; fallback to ElevenLabs if timeout
    - Rationale: Cost control (self-hosted = 90% cheaper than ElevenLabs for high volume); latency critical for user experience

15. **CRM Integration (Salesforce/HubSpot)** (Month 3, Week 3–4)
    - OAuth flow to authenticate with CRM
    - Bi-directional sync: create contact in Recall Touch → sync to CRM; CRM update → pull to Recall Touch
    - Map Recall Touch fields to CRM fields (phone → Phone, company_name → Company)
    - Webhook listener for CRM changes; pull opportunity + lead status
    - Link conversations + workflows to CRM opportunities (attribution)
    - Rationale: Sales teams live in CRM; without sync, Recall Touch is disconnected tool; integration is must-have for adoption

---

**"Never Lose a Customer to a Forgotten Follow-Up Again"**

**Variant 1: Benefit-Forward (Aggressive Growth Focus)**
"Turn Forgotten Contacts Into Closed Deals"
*Targets: Sales directors, revenue teams. Action-oriented. Result quantifiable.*

"Automated Follow-Ups That Actually Convert—In Minutes, Not Days"
*Targets: Solopreneurs, agencies. Speed = credibility. Emphasizes ease.*

**Variant 3: Problem-Agitation (Fear-Based)**
"Your Best Prospects Are Walking Away Right Now"
*Targets: High-performer mindset. Urgency + loss aversion. Creates cognitive dissonance.*

"Scale Your Revenue While You Sleep"
*Targets: Ambitious founders. Passive income positioning. Luxury feel.*

"The System Top Sales Teams Use to Never Miss a Deal"
*Targets: Enterprise/cautious buyers. Social proof embedded. Peer validation.*

## 4. HERO DEMO CONCEPT

### INTERACTIVE HERO DEMO MECHANICS

**Demo Type:** Animated, click-through experience (no video required on load)

**Demo Flow (3-Stage Interactive):**

**Stage 1: The Problem (0-2 seconds)**
- User's phone/screen shows a contact card: "Sarah Chen, Prospect, Last Contact: 23 Days Ago"
- Visual: Red indicator pulsing ("FORGOTTEN")
- Copy overlay: "Without Recall Touch, your best leads go dark..."
- Duration: Auto-plays or user clicks "Next"

**Stage 2: The Recall Touch Solution (2-4 seconds)**
- Screen transitions to Recall Touch interface
- Animated sequence: Contact card moves into smart inbox
- Algorithm visualization: Blue particle effects flow through timeline showing "optimal follow-up windows"
- Copy overlay: "We identify WHEN your prospect is most likely to engage..."
- Yellow highlight appears on contact card: "Perfect Follow-Up Moment: Tomorrow, 2:47 PM"

**Stage 3: The Outcome (4-6 seconds)**
- All three channels light up simultaneously:
  - Email icon + green checkmark ("Personalized email sent")
  - WhatsApp bubble + green checkmark ("SMS scheduled")
  - LinkedIn icon + green checkmark ("Connection request + note")
- Contact card updates: Status changes to "WARM LEAD — Responded in 3 hours"
- Copy overlay: "...and automatically execute at the right moment. Across every channel."
- Final frame: Green border around contact card, "3 New Replies Waiting"

**Interactive Elements:**
- Clickable arrow buttons to advance/retreat
- Pause button to inspect any frame
- "Try with your data" CTA appears at end (leads to sign-up flow)
- Mobile version: Simplified 2-stage version (Problem → Solution)

**Visual Design for Demo:**
- Dark background (charcoal gray #1a1a1a) with neon accent colors
- Blue for AI/automation elements
- Green for success/completion
- Red for problems/friction
- Typography: Clean, modern sans-serif (display: bold, body: regular weight)
- Micro-animations: Smooth easing (ease-out 0.4s) on all transitions
- Sound: Subtle "success" chime on completion (optional, toggleable)

**Conversion Purpose:** Demo reduces friction by showing outcome *before* asking for sign-up. Prospects understand value in 6 seconds. No reading required. Mobile-optimized to prevent scroll fatigue.

### SECTION 4: SOLUTION REVEAL SECTION

**Layout Description:**
- Full width, centered content
- Single column layout with centered max-width 900px container
- Background: Gradient from #252525 (top) to #1a1a1a (bottom, returning to hero tone)

**Feature 5: "Intelligent Sequences & Workflows" (Image Right)**

```
"Follow-up sequences aren't linear. They branch. They adapt.

Basic Workflow Example:
Day 0: Initial email send (you write it, Recall Touch times it)
Day 2: If no open, SMS reminder (short, punchy)
Day 4: If no reply, escalate to WhatsApp + LinkedIn
Day 6: If replied, offer a call. If ignored, pause and re-engage in 10 days.

Advanced Workflow Example (Intelligent Branching):
Day 0: Send email with 3 different subject lines (A/B/C test)
Day 2 (Branching):
  - If opened subject A → email 2 on topic A
  - If opened subject B → email 2 on topic B
  - If opened neither → SMS with different angle
Day 4 (Deeper Branching):
  - If replied with objection X → send objection-handling email
  - If clicked pricing link → send pricing proposal follow-up
  - If went silent → pause 5 days, then re-engagement sequence
Day 7+:
  - Responses feed into CRM. Sales rep takes over.
  - Non-responders enter nurture sequence.

Building Sequences:
Visual workflow builder (no coding). Drag-and-drop conditions. 
Pre-built templates for common use cases:
  • Cold outreach to warm prospect
  • Discovery call follow-up
  • Proposal sent, waiting on response
  • Demo request, no-show
  • Trial signup, no engagement

Control: You control all sequences. 100% customizable. 
Test and iterate until you find what works."

Stat Callout (bold, blue accent):

vs. linear, one-size-fits-all sequences."
```

---

**Example Calculations (Behind the Scenes):**
```
Formula 1: Additional Revenue Opportunity
= (Active Contacts × Follow-up Rate) × Deal Value 
  × (Response Rate Improvement % - baseline ~20%) 
  × Closure Rate Improvement %
= (500 × 0.65) × $15,000 × (0.35 × 0.20) × 0.28
= 325 contacts × $15,000 × 0.07 × 0.28
= ~$847,500

Formula 2: Hours Saved Per Year
= (Active Contacts × Follow-ups per year) × (5 minutes manual time per follow-up) / 60
= (500 × 3) × 5 / 60
= 1,500 × 5 / 60
= 125 hours × 3.3 (for other overhead: scheduling, tracking, updating CRM)
= ~412 hours per year

Formula 3: Sales Cycle Reduction
= Average industry baseline (typically 45 days) × 0.23 (23% reduction)
= 10.35 days saved
= Translates to 23% cycle time improvement

Formula 4: Monthly ROI
= (Additional Annual Revenue / 12) - Recall Touch Cost
= ($847,500 / 12) - $4,000
= $70,625 - $4,000
= $66,625 per month
= ~$2,847 per day revenue lift
```

---

**Visual/Design Notes:**
- Calculator inputs: Clean, minimal styling. Text fields with subtle borders (#3b82f6)
- Slider style: Blue accent color for active range, gray for inactive
- Results boxes: Grid layout (2x2 desktop, 1x4 mobile). Each box has left-border accent (4px, varies by color)
  - Box 1: Blue
  - Box 2: Green
  - Box 3: Orange
  - Box 4: Purple
- Big numbers: 48px, bold, white
- Labels: 14px, semibold, light gray
- Explanations: 12px, light gray, line-height 1.5
- Animation: Results fade in/update smoothly (0.3s) as inputs change
- Interactivity: Slider knobs glow blue on hover/focus
- Mobile: Inputs stack above results. Results stay visible as user scrolls (sticky/fixed option)

**Conversion Purpose:** Quantifies abstract benefits into concrete revenue numbers. Interactive element increases engagement (avg. time on page +3 min for interactives). Builds confidence before sign-up. ROI clarity = higher conversion rate. Target: 40%+ of visitors interact with calculator; 15%+ use it to completion.

**Table Legend (Below table):**
```
✓ = Fully supported / Best-in-class
⚠ = Limited / Add-on cost / Partial support
✗ = Not available / Not included

Note: Comparison based on public feature lists as of March 2025. 
Pricing varies by plan and annual commitment. See pricing page for details.
```

### SECTION 14: FAQ (10+ QUESTIONS)

**Layout Description:**
- Full width section with max-width 900px container
- Accordion-style expandable questions (all collapsed by default)
- Background: Light gray (#2a2a2a)
- Padding: 80px top/bottom, 40px sides
- Questions organized into 3 categories (collapsible tabs)

**Copy - FAQ Content:**

**Section Header:**
```
Headline (H2, 36px, white, centered):
"Questions? We Have Answers."

Subheadline (14px, gray, centered):
"Everything you need to know about Recall Touch. 
Can't find what you're looking for? 
Email support@recalltouch.com"
```

---

**FAQ Category 1: "Getting Started"**

**Q1: "How long does setup take?"**
```
A: "60 seconds. Here's what happens:
1. Connect your CRM (Salesforce, HubSpot, Pipedrive, etc.)
2. Import or sync your contact list
3. Choose a pre-built template or create a custom sequence
4. Click 'Activate'

Your follow-ups start running immediately. 
We have a 2-minute onboarding video if you prefer guided walkthrough."
```

**Q2: "Do I need to learn anything complicated?"**
```
A: "No. Most users figure it out in 5 minutes. 
If you can use Gmail and Slack, you can use Recall Touch.

We also offer:
• 2-minute video tutorials for each feature
• Live chat support (24/7)
• Webinars every Tuesday (how to set up sequences, optimize timing, etc.)

Enterprise customers get a dedicated onboarding specialist."
```

**Q3: "Is there a free trial?"**
```
A: "Yes. 14 days, full access, no credit card required.

You get:
• All Pro features (unlimited contacts, all channels, analytics)
• Full API access
• Email support

After 14 days, you're on your plan (or you can downgrade to free tier, 
limited to 100 contacts/month)."
```

**Q4: "What if I'm not technical?"**
```
A: "Recall Touch is built for non-technical users. 

No coding required. 
No CSV uploads required.
No complex configuration.

Our drag-and-drop sequence builder looks like a flowchart. 
Point, click, build. Done.

If you get stuck, our support team responds in <2 hours via chat."
```

---

**FAQ Category 2: "Features & Functionality"**

**Q5: "How does the timing algorithm work?"**
```
A: "Our AI analyzes 100+ signals for each contact:

• Historical engagement (when did they open/reply to your emails?)
• Role-based patterns (VPs typically check email 7-9 AM)
• Industry benchmarks (SaaS buyers more active Tuesday-Thursday)
• Seasonal factors (no follow-ups Dec 20-Jan 2)
• Sales cycle stage (early-stage vs. late-stage timing differs)
• External events (earnings calls, company news, holidays)

The algorithm outputs a 5-7 day window with 73% higher response probability 
vs. random timing.

It learns continuously: Every response refines predictions. 
Your system gets smarter every day."
```

**Q6: "Can I customize the follow-up messages?"**
```
A: "Absolutely. 100% customizable.

Every template is editable. You can:
• Rewrite the entire message
• Add custom personalization tokens ([Company_Revenue], [Decision_Maker], etc.)
• Use conditional logic (if they clicked link A, send message B)
• A/B test subject lines (our algorithm tests which performs better)
• Brand the emails (your logo, colors, signature)

We provide 100+ templates as starting points 
(by industry, deal stage, use case). 
But you own the copy completely."
```

**Q7: "What channels are supported?"**
```
A: "All major channels:

• Email (SMTP native, templates with tracking)
• SMS (Twilio integration)
• WhatsApp (Twilio integration)
• LinkedIn (native message + connection requests)

You can deploy across all four simultaneously 
(one follow-up, four channels, each optimized for medium).

More channels coming: In-app notifications, Slack, Teams, web push."
```

**Q8: "Does it integrate with my CRM?"**
```
A: "Yes. Native integrations with:

• Salesforce (activity logging, contact sync, custom fields)
• HubSpot (contact sync, email logging, deal tracking)
• Pipedrive (lead/deal tracking, email logging)
• Copper, Insightly, Freshsales, Attio (all similar feature parity)
• Plus 40+ more via Zapier & Make

Integration works both ways:
→ Recall Touch pulls contacts into your CRM automatically
← Responses sync back to your CRM (activities, emails logged)

Setup: 60 seconds. No code required."
```

---

**FAQ Category 3: "Security, Privacy & Compliance"**

**Q9: "Is my data secure?"**
```
A: "Yes. We're SOC 2 Type II certified.

Security measures:
• Bank-level encryption (AES-256 at rest, TLS in transit)
• Role-based access control (RBAC)
• Two-factor authentication
• IP whitelisting (for enterprise)
• Audit logs (all user actions tracked)
• 30-day backup retention
• Annual third-party security audit

For enterprise customers: Dedicated infrastructure option available.
Your data, completely isolated."
```

**Q10: "Is Recall Touch GDPR/CCPA compliant?"**
```
A: "Yes. We're fully GDPR and CCPA compliant.

What this means:
• Data processing agreements available (DPA)
• Contact deletion honored within 24 hours
• Privacy policy transparent and straightforward
• No third-party data broker integrations (we don't sell data)
• Right to data portability (export all contacts/history anytime)

We do NOT:
• Store passwords or security tokens
• Share contact data with third parties
• Use contact data for training models
• Sell contact lists

If you're in EU/UK: We use AWS EU data centers (Ireland). 
US: AWS US-East (Virginia)."
```

---

```
Option 1: Upgrade to paid plan (Solo $200/mo, Team $500+/mo, Enterprise custom)
Option 2: Downgrade to free tier (100 contacts/month, email-only, no sequences)
Option 3: Cancel (no penalty, no questions asked)

Billing: Monthly or annual (annual gets 2 months free).
Always cancel anytime.
No long-term contracts (except enterprise)."
```

```
Solo: $200/month
• 1 user
• Up to 1K contacts

• Email + SMS

Team: $500-2000/month (depending on number of users)
• 2-20 users
• Unlimited contacts
• Unlimited sequences
• All channels (email, SMS, WhatsApp, LinkedIn)
• Real-time dashboard

Enterprise: Custom (based on volume, team size, requirements)
• 50+ users
• Custom infrastructure
• API access
• Dedicated success manager
• Custom integrations

No per-contact fees. 
No per-email fees.
No hidden charges."
```

```
Annual pricing:
Solo: $2,400/year (saves $400 vs. monthly)

Plus: Enterprise qualifying customers get custom discounts based on volume."
```

## 6. TRUST ELEMENTS STRATEGY

**Overview:**
Trust elements are distributed throughout the page to reduce buyer hesitation at each stage of the funnel.

**Trust Element Placement Map:**

**Section 2 (Trust Bar):** Concentration of credibility signals
- Customer count badge (500+ teams)
- Star rating (4.9/5)
- Uptime badge (99.9% SLA)
- Customer logos (recognizable brands)
- Enterprise marker (Fortune 500 teams use us)
- Certifications (SOC 2 Type II)

**Section 4 (Solution Reveal):** Mechanism clarity
- Three pillars explain *how* (not just *that*) Recall Touch works
- Reduces perceived risk of hidden complexity

**Section 8 (ROI Calculator):** Proof through math
- Real data from 500+ teams
- Formula transparency
- Removes risk of unproven results

**Section 10 (Social Proof):**
- Testimonial carousel: Peer validation (similar-size companies)
- Case studies with detailed metrics: Specific, auditable proof
- Real names (when possible) vs. anonymized (for competitive sensitivity)

**Section 12 (Comparison):**
- Honest comparison (show where competitors are better)
- Builds credibility through transparency
- Direct head-to-head mitigates bias concern

**Section 14 (FAQ):**
- Security/compliance questions answered in detail (builds trust for security-concerned buyers)
- Support structure transparency (shows we're here to help, not just sell)

**Section 16 (Footer):**
- Trust badges (SOC 2, GDPR, CCPA, ISO) 
- Links to detailed security/privacy docs
- Data Processing Agreement availability

---

## 7. INTEGRATIONS STRIP COPY (DETAILED)

**Headline Options:**
- "Works with 50+ tools your team already loves"
- "Built for your existing tech stack"
- "Integrates with tools you use every day"

**Subheadline Options:**
- "No rip-and-replace. No learning new tools. Recall Touch fits seamlessly into your workflow."
- "Recall Touch connects to Salesforce, HubSpot, Gmail, Slack, Zapier, and 45+ others."
- "Whether you use Salesforce or a spreadsheet, we integrate with your tools."

**Integration Messaging Philosophy:**
The goal is to eliminate one major objection: "Will this work with our CRM/email/tools?"

By showing logos of tools prospects already know/use, we create instant credibility and reduce perceived friction.

**Native Integration Copy (Sample):**
```
"Native integrations with Salesforce, HubSpot, and Pipedrive mean 
your contacts sync automatically. Responses log instantly to your CRM. 
Everything stays in sync, all the time. 
No manual data entry. No duplicate records. No broken processes."
```

**API/Zapier Fallback Copy:**
```
"Using a less common CRM or tool? 
Our full REST API and Zapier integration supports 1000+ applications. 
If you can think of a tool, we probably integrate with it 
(or can custom-build a connector for enterprise customers)."
```

---

## 8. ALTERNATIVE HEADLINE ROUTES (3 DISTINCT APPROACHES)

### ROUTE 1: EMOTIONAL/ASPIRATIONAL
**Primary Headline:** "Scale Your Revenue While You Sleep"
**Subheadline:** "Automated follow-ups that work 24/7. Your sales rep's dream: deals closing while you focus on what matters."

**Pros:** Aspirational, memorable, action-oriented
**Cons:** May feel unrealistic to cynical buyers; doesn't explain *what* the product is
**Best for:** Solopreneurs, ambitious founders, growth mindset audience
**Variations:** 
- "Grow Your Pipeline Without Growing Your Team"
- "Close More Deals—Without the Sales Admin"

---

### ROUTE 2: PROBLEM-AGITATION (PAIN-FIRST)
**Primary Headline:** "Your Best Prospects Are Walking Away Right Now"
**Subheadline:** "Without systematic follow-ups, 60% of qualified deals go cold. Recall Touch stops that."

**Pros:** Triggers urgency, creates FOMO, highly specific
**Cons:** Negative tone may turn off confident/successful reps
**Best for:** Mid-market sales managers, quota-driven reps, risk-aware buyers
**Variations:**
- "Every Day Without a Follow-Up Is Lost Revenue"
- "Your Sales Cycle Is Broken (Here's How to Fix It)"
- "You're Leaving $847K on the Table"

---

### ROUTE 3: TRUST/AUTHORITY-FIRST
**Primary Headline:** "The Follow-Up System Top Sales Teams Depend On"
**Subheadline:** "500+ teams at growing companies use Recall Touch to close more deals, faster. Join them."

**Pros:** Social proof embedded, lowers perceived risk, attracts quality leads
**Cons:** May feel derivative to non-followers; less differentiated
**Best for:** Enterprise buyers, cautious decision-makers, B2B committees
**Variations:**
- "How Leading Sales Teams Close 35% More Deals"
- "The All-In-One Follow-Up System That Powers Growth"

---

## 9. ALTERNATIVE CTA VARIANTS (5+)

### CTA VARIANT 1: COMMITMENT-FORWARD
**Button Text:** "Start Free 14-Day Trial"
**Color:** Gradient blue-to-purple
**Positioning:** Hero, Section 4, Section 15, Footer
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 8-12% CTR (strong, but requires confidence)
**Best for:** Prospects ready to commit; product-confident

### CTA VARIANT 2: LOW-FRICTION DEMO
**Button Text:** "Watch 2-Minute Demo"
**Style:** Ghost/outline button
**Positioning:** Hero secondary, Section 5, Section 7
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 15-22% CTR (higher engagement, lower commitment)
**Best for:** Exploratory prospects; visual learners

---

### CTA VARIANT 3: SCARCITY/URGENCY
**Button Text:** "Claim Your Spot" or "Get Early Access"
**Color:** Red or orange accent (urgency color)
**Positioning:** Consider for high-traffic pages; use sparingly to avoid fatigue
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 6-9% CTR (urgency works, but can feel gimmicky)
**Best for:** Limited-time offers; feature launches; time-sensitive messaging

---

### CTA VARIANT 4: CONSULTATION/PERSONAL TOUCH
**Button Text:** "Schedule a Personal Demo" or "Talk to a Specialist"
**Style:** Solid button, warm color (teal or green)
**Positioning:** Enterprise sections, Section 6 (Team/Enterprise tabs), comparison table
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 3-6% CTR (lower volume, higher quality leads)
**Best for:** Enterprise buyers; complex requirements; white-glove buyers

---

### CTA VARIANT 5: SOCIAL PROOF + COMMITMENT
**Button Text:** "Join 500+ Teams Using Recall Touch"
**Style:** Solid gradient button with badge
**Positioning:** Hero, final CTA, high-traffic sections
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 9-13% CTR (combines commitment + FOMO)
**Best for:** Prospect who are FOMO-driven or validation-seeking

---

### CTA VARIANT 6: BENEFIT-IN-BUTTON
**Button Text:** "Increase My Pipeline by 35%"
**Style:** Solid green button
**Positioning:** ROI calculator, feature sections
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 7-11% CTR (outcome-focused, aspirational)
**Best for:** ROI-conscious buyers; metrics-driven audience

---

### CTA VARIANT 7: FRICTION REDUCER
**Button Text:** "Get Started Free (No CC)"
**Style:** Solid blue button
**Positioning:** Hero, early sections, mobile CTAs
**Conversion Rate Profile:** 10-14% CTR (explicit objection removal)
**Best for:** Risk-averse prospects; first-time trials

## 10. DESIGN TONE NOTES

### COLOR PALETTE

**Primary Colors:**
- Hero Blue: #3b82f6 (tech, trust, intelligence)
- Dark Background: #1a1a1a (premium, sleek, focus)
- Accent Purple: #a855f7 (innovation, forward-thinking)
- Success Green: #10b981 (growth, positive outcomes)

**Secondary Colors:**
- Warning Orange: #f59e0b (urgency, attention)
- Error Red: #ef4444 (problem states, warnings)
- Neutral Gray: #a8a8a8 (body text, secondary info)
- Light Gray: #d4d4d4 (primary text on dark)

**Reasoning:** Dark background conveys premium, tech-forward positioning (like Slack, Figma, Linear). Blue + purple combo = tech credibility. Green = growth messaging aligns with revenue focus.

---

### TYPOGRAPHY

**Headlines (H1, H2, H3):**
- Font family: Inter, Outfit, or similar modern sans-serif
- Weight: Bold (700) for H1, Semibold (600) for H2/H3
- Sizing: 64px (H1, hero) → 56px (mobile), 36px (H2), 28px (H3)
- Line height: 1.2 (tight, modern feel)
- Letter spacing: -0.02em (headlines slightly compressed for sophistication)

**Body Text:**
- Font family: Same as headlines (consistency)
- Weight: Regular (400) for body, Semibold (600) for callouts
- Sizing: 16px (large body), 14px (standard), 12px (small/caption)
- Line height: 1.6-1.8 (readable, breathing room)
- Letter spacing: 0 (neutral)

**Rationale:** Sans-serif throughout = modern, approachable. Consistent font family = cohesive, premium feel. Bold headlines + regular body = hierarchy clarity.

---

### SPACING & LAYOUT

**Vertical Spacing:**
- Section padding: 60-80px top/bottom (generous breathing room)
- Content gaps: 40px (desktop), 24px (tablet), 16px (mobile)
- Line spacing: 1.6-1.8 for body text (readable)

**Horizontal Spacing:**
- Max-width containers: 1200px (desktop), scales down responsively
- Side padding: 40px (desktop), 24px (tablet), 16px (mobile)
- Column gaps: 30-40px (grid layouts)

**Rationale:** Generous spacing = premium feel. Breathing room prevents overwhelming. Responsive scaling maintains proportions.

---

### PREMIUM FEEL TECHNIQUES

1. **Whitespace:** Use negative space heavily. Don't cram content.
2. **Subtle Shadows:** Box-shadow: 0 4px 12px rgba(0,0,0,0.15) on cards (depth without overdone)
3. **Rounded Corners:** 8px border-radius on cards, 12px on larger blocks (modern, not sharp)
4. **Gradients:** Use sparingly. Blue-to-purple on hero CTA (sophisticated, not garish)
5. **Typography:** Bold headlines + regular body, generous line-height (luxury feel)
6. **Color Restraint:** Limit palette to 3-4 accent colors (sophistication)
7. **Animation:** Smooth, subtle micro-interactions (0.2-0.4s ease-out, not flashy)
8. **Photography/Imagery:** High-quality, professional (not stock photography where possible; custom illustrations preferred)

---

### DARK MODE APPROACH

**Current Strategy:** Homepage is in dark mode by default (#1a1a1a background).

**Light Mode (If offered as toggle):**
- Background: Off-white (#f9fafb)
- Text: Dark gray (#1a1a1a)
- Accents: Same (blue #3b82f6, purple #a855f7, etc.)
- Cards: White (#ffffff) with subtle border (#e5e7eb)
- Shadows: Same box-shadows, but with lighter rgba values (rgba(0,0,0,0.08) instead of 0.15)

**Rationale:** Dark mode = default (modern, premium, reduces eye strain). Light mode as toggle for accessibility/preference.

---

### ANIMATION PHILOSOPHY

**Core Principles:**
1. **Purpose:** Every animation should serve UX (clarify interaction, provide feedback, guide attention)
2. **Subtlety:** 0.2-0.4s duration. Ease-out easing (deceleration, natural feel)
3. **Restraint:** Don't animate everything. Animate key interactions (hover, click, scroll reveal)
4. **Performance:** Use CSS transforms + opacity (GPU-accelerated, 60fps)
5. **Accessibility:** Respect `prefers-reduced-motion` media query (disable for users who prefer no motion)

**Specific Animations:**
- Button hover: Lift (translateY -2px) + brightness (+5%) over 0.2s
- Card hover: Lift (translateY -4px) + glow (box-shadow increase) over 0.2s
- Scroll reveal: Fade in (opacity 0 → 1) + slide up (translateY 20px → 0) over 0.3s, staggered
- Carousel transition: Fade + slide (new content slides in from right as old fades out) over 0.4s
- Interactive elements (inputs, sliders): Subtle glow on focus (box-shadow: 0 0 8px rgba(59,130,246,0.5))

**Mobile Considerations:**
- Reduce animation on mobile (touch interactions don't benefit from hover states)
- Keep scroll animations (they're still valuable for attention guidance)
- Disable parallax on mobile (can cause jank on lower-end devices)

---

### MOBILE CONSIDERATIONS

**Responsive Breakpoints:**
- Desktop: > 1024px
- Tablet: 768px - 1024px
- Mobile: < 768px

**Mobile-Specific Optimizations:**

**Hero Section:**
- Stack text + demo vertically
- CTAs full-width, stacked vertically
- Text scales down (56px headline, 18px subheadline)
- Demo area shrinks (mobile-optimized version)

**Feature Showcase:**
- 2-column grid on tablet, single column on mobile
- Images scale responsively
- Text remains readable (min font size 14px)

**Forms/Inputs:**
- Full-width on mobile
- Large touch targets (min 48px height)
- Numeric keyboard for number inputs (type="number")
- Date picker for date inputs (type="date")

**Navigation:**
- Sticky header on scroll (mobile nav always accessible)
- Hamburger menu for mobile (if nav exists in header)

**Tables:**
- Convert to 2-column format or horizontal scroll on mobile
- Stack rows with labels (make data scannable)

**CTAs:**
- Full-width button on mobile
- Sticky footer CTA (always visible, doesn't disappear on scroll)
- Larger touch targets (48px min height)

**Performance:**
- Lazy load images (load on scroll/viewport)
- Optimize for Core Web Vitals (LCP < 2.5s, CLS < 0.1, FID < 100ms)
- Minify CSS/JS
- Use WEBP images (with fallback to JPG)

---

**Summary Tone:**
The homepage should feel premium, modern, and trustworthy. Dark background + bold typography + generous spacing = sophistication. Animation is subtle and purposeful, not gratuitous. Mobile-first thinking ensures responsiveness without compromising desktop elegance.
